Navy Demands Repair Fees for Ships

Misunderstanding Occurs on the Fuhai Patrol Ship

Armed Navy Sails to the Ship to Demand Payment

Fuhai Soldiers Fire Live Ammunition as a Demonstration

The Zhejiang District Marine Fisheries Administration of the Ministry of Industry entrusted the Fuhai patrol ship of the bureau to the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Ministry of Navy for repairs last year. Yesterday at 1:00 p.m., the naval authorities, because the ship had accumulated repair fees that had not been paid, sent special personnel accompanied by guards to the ship to demand payment. At the same time, the Fuhai patrol ship also believed that the Fisheries Administration owed soldiers' salaries for five and a half months, and their lives could not be maintained. Seeing the navy fully armed and in a turbulent situation, they thought they were going to confiscate their weapons, so they fired a shot of live ammunition into the water as a demonstration. At the same time, they ordered special security and refused to allow boarding. The naval side was afraid of causing trouble, so they left immediately and waited for negotiations. The details are recorded separately below:

Entrusting Repair of Patrol Ship

The Fisheries Administration has a Fuhai patrol ship, which specializes in patrolling and protecting fishing boats in areas such as Wenzhou and Taizhou. Previously, due to damage to the hull, it was entrusted to the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Ministry of Navy for repairs last year. It has accumulated more than 20,000 yuan in repair fees. Personnel have been sent to the bureau many times to collect the money, but due to the bureau's financial difficulties, successive directors have been unable to pay it off and have delayed until now, still not paid in full.

Navy Demands Payment

The Jiangnan Shipyard believes that it is wrong for the bureau to not return the owed money for a long time, and the shipyard itself has also felt financially strapped in recent years. Therefore, yesterday at 1:00 p.m., the Naval First Fleet Command sent Wang Wenbo, platoon leader of the first platoon of the third company of the Naval Guard Battalion, and Liu Zhaopu, platoon leader of the third platoon, leading more than 20 guards, on the Jiangnan and Jiangkang small launches of the Naval Water Patrol Team to the Fuhai patrol ship to demand the owed payment.

Misunderstanding Occurs

The Fisheries Administration's current fishery protection patrol ships docked in this port include the Fuhai and Haiying, both docked in the Huangpu River at Guanhua Bridge in Nanshi. When the Jiangnan and Jiangkang small launches carrying Wang and Liu, the two platoon leaders of the Navy, arrived at the Fuhai patrol ship at about 2:00 p.m., about ten feet apart, Platoon Leader Wang stood up from the cabin of the Jiangnan launch, intending to explain the purpose of their visit to the personnel of the Fuhai patrol ship, but unfortunately, a misunderstanding occurred.

Firing One Shot

At that time, the Fuhai patrol ship misunderstood the intention and fired a shot of live ammunition into the water as a demonstration with a Mauser pistol. At the same time, the machine gun cover at the bow of the ship was removed, and serious precautions were taken to prevent naval soldiers from boarding. At the same time, Wang and Liu, the two platoon leaders of the Navy, were afraid that the situation would escalate, and that the Pujiang River was a major thoroughfare for merchant ships, and the Nisshin Company also had three ships docked nearby. A slight carelessness could lead to diplomatic disputes. Therefore, they waved to signal the Hai'an ship, and at the same time restrained the guards, not allowing them to retaliate. After a stalemate of about ten minutes, the two small naval launches sailed away, temporarily docked at the nearby Datong Wharf, and quickly reported to Ye Baoqi, the battalion commander of the Naval Guard Battalion, and forwarded it to Commander Chen Jiliang for review.

Ye's Remarks

After the incident, this reporter made a special trip to meet with Ye Baoqi, the battalion commander of the Naval Guard Battalion. According to his remarks, today he was ordered by the commander to send Wang and Liu, the two platoon leaders, to lead the guards on small launches to the Fuhai patrol ship to discuss official business. Unexpectedly, as soon as the two small launches sailed close to the ship, the ship fired live ammunition without asking the reason, hitting the outside of the engine room of the Jiangnan launch. It then tried to fire a machine gun. The situation at that time was incomprehensible. Fortunately, the guards under his command were still aware of the overall situation and did not retaliate, otherwise the traffic would be heavy in that area, and the consequences would be unimaginable. After checking, the officers and soldiers of this army, no matter where they go, or to foreign warships, can pass with guards. However, the ship fired live ammunition immediately without asking about the situation, which is really strange. The situation has now been reported to the command, and we will wait for the command's orders to deal with it, he said.

Fuhai's Reasons

This newspaper reporter went to Datong Wharf in Nanshi at 10:00 p.m. last night to investigate. The two small naval launches were no longer there. He then took a sampan to the Fuhai patrol ship docked in the Pujiang River to inquire. When approaching, the Fuhai soldiers questioned with guns, and the situation was indeed extremely serious. According to the soldiers, the captain of the Fuhai ship is Guo Wei, and there are more than fifty soldiers. The Fisheries Bureau has owed wages for five and a half months, and the soldiers' lives are really unsustainable. This afternoon (that is, yesterday), the navy drove two small launches close, and the situation was turbulent, ordering this ship to lower the flag. We thought that because the arrears were not paid, they still wanted to take the opportunity to come on board and confiscate our weapons. For self-defense, we fired a shot of live ammunition into the water as a demonstration and did not allow them to board the ship. The navy had no choice but to sail away immediately. As for the payment collection, it should be directly contacted with the Fisheries Administration. How can there be any reason to negotiate with this ship?

Xia Tengfei's Statement

The Beiping Chang Tengfei telecommunications company stated to the Shen Bao News, Times News, and China News: Recently, I read in the Times News that I will definitely go to Shanghai on [day of the week] to participate in the Northeast Army Joint Communications Office and contact various parties for assistance, etc. After investigating, the joint communications office in Shanghai was originally the general agency for mutual communication between representatives of the various Volunteer Armies and has no other function. Moreover, all the supplies for our army are currently being handled by Chairman Cheng. I am staying in Beiping on official business and have not gone south. If there is any false atmosphere, I will not admit it. I am deeply afraid that rumors from afar are untrue, so I specially telegraph this statement. I hope you will take note of it. Northeast People's National Salvation Army Deputy Commander Feng Zhanhai Representative Xia Tengfei kowtows.

Charity Association Joint Meeting Minutes

Separate Acknowledgement of Calligraphy, Paintings, Antiques, and Lottery Tickets

Letter Asking About Hartung's Million-Dollar Charitable Donation

It's Cold and the Shelters Are Crowded

The Shanghai Charity Association held a temporary meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 p.m. Those who attended were Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, and representatives from the Zanye Gongyi Association, Huazhong Shantang, Shanghai Orphanage, Hunan Charity Association, Lianyi Shan Society, Shenzhou Hospital, Shanghai Puji Shan Society, Guangyi Shantang, Relief Women's Society, Pushan Villa, Shanghai Disabled Persons' Home, Shanghai Hospital, Yimiao Board of Directors, Gongji Shantang, Fushan Hall, Renji Shantang, Renji Nursery, and other representatives, more than twenty people. Recently, major benefactors have donated a large number of calligraphy, paintings, antiques, and various items, which are very valuable. The Lianyi Shan Society is now printing lottery tickets, each ticket is ten yuan, that is, the aforementioned donations will be publicly drawn on January 9, 22 at the Lake Society. All the donations received will be used to aid

Northeast refugees. The Lianyi Shan Society sent 500 lottery tickets the day before yesterday, asking each charitable organization to distribute them as much as possible to maintain the good deed. These tickets must be sent to the association for compilation before the lottery draw. If the lottery tickets cannot be sold out, they must also be returned to the association before the lottery draw, and will not be returned after the deadline. Passed. 2) Wang Junsheng of Pushan Villa proposed that Mr. Xu Qianlin and Xie Hengchu reported last summer that Hartung had passed away and planned to withdraw one million from his estate and allocate it to various charitable organizations to specifically handle charitable undertakings. The association was consulted to invite various charitable organizations to prepare sacrifices and go to mourn. Now that more than a year has passed, there is no news about the appropriation. It is not worth arguing whether each charitable organization can obtain the money or not, but the current social situation is that there are more and more poor people and more and more unemployed people. If the Hartung family can sincerely withdraw huge sums of money, or specifically run a poor people's factory, or expand the existing local businesses separately to provide relief, it is also what the colleagues hope for. Should the case be urged and inquired? It was decided that the association would prepare a letter to inquire Mr. Lin and Hengchu and then consider the use of the appropriation amount. Passed. 3) The chairman reported that the temporary shelters run by the association opened the first shelter on the 10th of this month, at the Chaozhou Guild Hall in the South Railway Station, the second at the Dawang Temple on Dawangmiao Street, and the third at the Jiangxi Guild Hall on Xiaopudu Street. Recently, the weather has turned cold suddenly, and poor people have flocked in. Currently, more than 1,600 people have been accommodated, and each shelter is about to be full. We are looking for other houses to prepare for the fourth and fifth shelters. The shelters urgently need funds. It is hoped that the donations acknowledged by various groups in the last meeting will be handed in as soon as possible for expenditure.

China Merchants Bureau Recent News

Establishment of Audit Department

In order to reorganize the bureau's affairs and implement supervisory duties, the China Merchants Bureau's Supervisory Board held its fourth Supervisory Board meeting. The attending supervisors, Lu Jianquan, Yu Qiaqing, etc., agreed to organize an audit department, whose task is to audit the accounts of the general and branch bureaus and boat companies, etc. Li Yunliang, the former Hankou Bureau Director and Business Section Chief of the bureau, has been hired to serve. Two deputy auditors will also be announced soon. The general audit department has already been organized by Mr. Li yesterday.

Zhen Floating Dock Bidding

The Zhenjiang Lotus Pond floating dock, which has been occupied by the British trading company Jardine Matheson for a long time, has now been negotiated and recovered. For the convenience of upper and lower Yangtze River ships berthing, the Shipping Section has moved the bureau's Zhen dock to Lotus Pond. However, at the beginning of the relocation, the construction of all the square boats and the addition of the trestle bridge are huge projects. Section Chief Zhao Yuntai, in order to seek truth from facts, has specially invited bids for construction and has drafted the regulations and will announce the bidding soon.

Yangtze River Ship Resumes Service

The Yangtze River ships of the bureau were suspended in late last month, and the difference was that they had been used for a full month, which inevitably affected business. Yesterday, the bureau received a telegram from Beijing that the Yangtze River ships Jiangda and Jiangtian, which had been suspended for a long time, were all released and allowed to resume operations as usual from tomorrow.

China Merchants Bureau

Shareholder Representatives Go to Beijing to Petition

Request the Third Plenary Session to Revoke the Nationalization Original Case

The China Merchants Bureau Shareholders' Rights Maintenance Association believes that the government's nationalization of the bureau this time is in conflict with the Regulations on Supervision of Private Public Utilities promulgated in December of the 18th year of the Republic of China. Therefore, after a preparatory meeting, it was decided to send representatives to Beijing to submit a petition to the Third Plenary Session to revoke the original case in which the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Transportation decided to take the China Merchants Bureau into state ownership. The representatives, Li Zhengwu, Li Cishan, Yu Gumin, and others, took the overnight express train to Beijing last night and will visit the central members today to request relief. The original presentation is recorded below: It is presented for the matter of petitioning. The case investigates the meeting of the Executive Yuan on November 8 this year, which was requested by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Transportation to nationalize the China Merchants Bureau, reorganize the supervisory office into a board of directors, and establish a general manager. All stocks shall be taken into state ownership at a price of fifty taels of standard silver per set, determined by the average market price of the past three years, thirty taels, six qian, and six fen per set, etc., which was passed after deliberation and submitted to the Central Political Council for approval. Subsequently, the competent department sent personnel to take over the cases. We believe that the China Merchants Bureau is the largest private public utility in our country. Tracing its evolution, there have been changes, and the people's livelihood and navigation rights are of great importance. If the government needs to innovate, it should deliberate at length. Since it is under party rule, it should proceed according to law. The Regulations on Supervision of Private Public Utilities were promulgated in December of the 18th year of the Republic of China and have not been abolished. Item 5 of Article 2 of the same regulations states that shipping business is one of the public utilities. Article 14 also states that after a private public utility has been in operation for 30 years, the supervisory authority may collect it for public operation after preparing the price, but must notify one year in advance. Item 2 of the same article states that private public utilities established before the implementation of these regulations may be allowed to apply the preceding provisions after 30 years of implementation of these regulations and be collected for public operation. Article 15 also states that when a private public utility is collected for public operation, it shall be paid according to the total amount of its existing assets. The price assessed by the 〇 experts. Item 2 of the same article states that if there is any objection to the evaluation in the preceding paragraph, the court in the area shall send three members, and the local autonomous organization and the chamber of commerce shall each send two members to form an evaluation committee to examine and approve it, etc. The legislation is detailed, and China and foreign countries have everything. In this case, the competent departments handled the nationalization case of the China Merchants Bureau. After the administrative deliberation was passed, personnel were immediately sent to take over without considering the statutory time limit or giving prior notice. The oldest and largest private public utility was taken into state ownership within less than ten days. The pricing method is based on the average market price of the stock in the most recent three years, which is obviously contrary to the statutory regulations of assessing and paying according to the current assets. As for the personnel participating in the evaluation, what legal qualifications they have, there is no basis in law. According to the Regulations on Supervision of Private Public Utilities, it has not been three years since the promulgation. According to the regulations, the life of the China Merchants Bureau is still 27 years. According to the general practice of constitutional countries, orders cannot change the law. None of the administrative punishments imposed by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Transportation this time are in line with the legal text. I don't know where the dignity of the law and the credibility of the country are placed. Even in terms of facts and reasons, the total assets of the China Merchants Bureau are worth no less than 70 million taels, and the price offered by the authorities is less than 4% of the actual value of each share. How can it be fair? The public is panicked, and there is no way to get relief. The authorities are determined to innovate, and businessmen are happy to follow, but the prestige of the national law is concerned, and they dare not remain silent. I hope that the钧 Council will comprehensively consider the national economy and observe the people's livelihood. I dare to appeal based on the facts and ask the General Assembly to approve the revocation of the original case in which the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Transportation decided to take the China Merchants Bureau into state ownership, and to handle it in accordance with the Regulations on Supervision of Private Public Utilities, so as to correct the administration on the right track and maintain the rule of law forever. Not only is it the fortune of the public, but it is also the glory of the party and the country. It is reasonable to petition based on the facts. I beg you to examine and implement it. This is presented to the Fourth Session of the Third Central Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang. Petitioners: China Merchants Bureau Shareholder Representatives Li Zhengwu, Li Cishan, Yu Gumin.

Pengpu District

Part of the Petition Representatives Return to Shanghai

Representatives Remaining in Beijing Continue to Petition to the Administrative Supervision

All the villagers in Wangjiajing, Zhaojia Garden, Zhuxiang, and other villages in Pengpu District have repeatedly petitioned various party and government agencies because the Ministry of Railways' expropriation of the people's land there is detrimental to the people's livelihood, but to no avail. Therefore, on the morning of the 13th, more than ten villagers went to the Railway Bureau to request a car to go to Beijing, intending to petition the Third Plenary Session. Later, because the Railway Bureau prevented them from getting on the car, there was a disturbance. After Wen Hongen of the Public Security Bureau mediated, he gave ten people round-trip free tickets, and the rest bought their own tickets before it was resolved. At that time, thirty representatives, including Hou Xuanqing, Zhao Wenxiu, Zhao Zhixing, Hou Shizhang, Zhang Zhongxiang, etc., were elected and took a car to Beijing that night. They arrived in Beijing the next morning. Wu, the section chief of the Xiaguan Police Section, was ordered by Ma, the director of the Shanghai Police Department, to forcibly cancel the free tickets for returning to Shanghai. After several negotiations, there were no results. The representatives believed that since the free tickets were issued through the mediation of Director Wen, Director Ma unreasonably confiscated them, which was obviously intentional to make things difficult. They telegraphed Director Wen for relief. Later, they received a reply from Director Wen, saying that he had agreed with Director Chen and telegraphed the Xiaguan stationmaster to check. The details are recorded below:

Chairman of the Assembly Endorses

At about 10:00 a.m. on the 15th, all the representatives carried submissions, declarations, maps, etc. to the Third Plenary Session to petition. Because the Third Plenary Session only held the opening ceremony that day and had already adjourned, and the Secretariat of the Assembly had not been established, there were no responsible personnel, so they left. At 12:00 noon, they hosted reporters from Beijing and Shanghai at the Jinlingchun Restaurant in Fuzimiao, asking for sympathy and assistance. On the 12th, the Executive Yuan had previously resolved that this case should be planned by the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Military Affairs, and the Ministry of Industry in consultation with the Zhen Department. Therefore, they prepared a submission and went to the Ministry of Military Affairs at 9:00 a.m. to petition, requesting Minister He to find a way to provide relief. Li Shiquan of the Protocol Section met with them and promised to convey it to the minister and handle it impartially. At 10:00 a.m., they went to the Ministry of Industry to make the same request. Li Pingheng, the director of the Labor Division, met with them and promised to consult with the responsible personnel of the three departments to discuss a proper solution or send personnel to Shanghai to investigate the actual truth. At 11:00 a.m., they went to the Ministry of Interior. Secretary Chen met with them and said that he expressed sympathy for the intentions of the people. The Ministry of Interior mainly focuses on the urgent use of land expropriated from the people, and the large-scale plan in the future cannot be fully collected before application, causing heavy losses to the people, etc. At 3:00 p.m., they returned to the Third Plenary Session to petition. Ye Shizhi of the Secretariat met with the representatives Hou Xuanqing, Zhao Wenxiu, and Hou Shizhang, and told them that the Third Plenary Session had submitted this case to the Presidium. He was instructed by the chairman of the assembly to order the Executive Yuan to handle the case carefully and jointly, and also showed the endorsement of Ding Weifen and Ju Zheng, the chairman of the assembly that day. The representatives then left at about 4:00 p.m.

Some Representatives Return to Shanghai

The representatives believed that the petition to the Third Plenary Session had temporarily come to an end. Therefore, some representatives, including Zhao Wenxiu, Tao Wenyuan, Zhao Zhixing, and Wang Futing, returned to Shanghai yesterday morning to report the progress. The representatives remaining in Beijing, Hou Xuanqing, Zhao Youting, Hou Shizhang, Zhang Zhongxiang, Tao Zhigang, etc., plan to petition the Executive Yuan and the Control Yuan again. It is heard that the villagers were outraged by Director Ma's unwarranted difficulty and have petitioned the Railway Department Administration to dismiss him and investigate him.

Dragon Zhang Paper Mill Labor Strike Immediately Ceased

Party and Government Persuasion Led to Resumption of Work Yesterday Afternoon

Labor-Management Dispute Awaiting Mediation

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Long Zhang Paper Mill on Longhua Road is large-scale and employs over eight hundred male and female workers. The female rag pickers opposed the dismissal of workers and fines, and went on strike on the previous day. Yesterday, after persuasion from party and government agencies, they resumed work in the afternoon and await mediation. The details are as follows:

(Going on Strike Together) About three hundred long-term and temporary workers in the rag-picking section of the Long Zhang Mill, when leaving work at 12:00 noon on the 15th, female worker number 141 refused to be inspected by the foreman, resulting in a dispute. After starting work at 1:00 p.m., the female worker clashed with the foreman again, causing minor injuries to both sides. The factory director immediately announced the dismissal of the female worker. On the 16th, all the female workers in the rag-picking section went on strike together. After being notified, the First District Paper Industry Union immediately advised the workers to resume work, but to no avail. The striking female workers put forward: 1) a request to reinstate worker number 141; 2) opposition to the factory's fines. The union believed that the extension of the strike in the rag-picking section would lead to a shortage of raw materials and that other departments would inevitably have to stop working as a result. It immediately petitioned the Municipal Party Department's Social Affairs Bureau for swift mediation.

(Persuasion to Resume Work) After being notified, the Municipal Party Department dispatched Zhao Erchang, a staff member of the Training Section, at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, together with Zhu Guilin, a mediator from the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, to try to mediate the situation. They also summoned the union and the female workers to persuade them. As a result, all the female workers resumed work at the factory at 1:00 p.m. The issue of worker number 141 and the factory's fines will be settled by party and government agencies in accordance with the law. The striking female workers expressed their satisfaction, and work was fully resumed at 1:00 p.m.

Shanghai South Motor Company Declares Bankruptcy

According to a Shen Shi Telegraph Agency local news report, the Huashang Shanghai South Public Motor Company, due to poor business, declared a temporary suspension of operations in September of this year and entrusted accountant Jiang Wanping to clear its accounts. It is now learned that accountant Jiang has completed the clearing and has submitted the clearing results, along with the balance sheet, to the Shanghai Local Court for a declaration of bankruptcy. He requested that bankruptcy trustees be appointed in accordance with the provisions of the Company Law Liquidation Regulations in order to begin auctioning off the remaining assets to repay creditors. It is reported that the company's total loss is more than 161,000 yuan, of which the remaining assets are valued at more than 100,000 yuan, leaving a balance of more than 60,000 yuan, which cannot be repaid because the shareholders have limited liability.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables Jiangsu Province to Dredge the River Dams in Northern Jiangsu

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce cabled the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction yesterday, requesting the dredging of the river dams in the Yunhe River in northern Jiangsu to maintain cargo transport. The original text reads: "To the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction: On the 16th of this month, the Shanghai Grain, Oilcake, and Noodle Industry Association wrote to inform us that according to letters from our fellow traders and distant branches, merchants in northern Jiangsu have reported that due to the prolonged drought, the water level in the Yunhe River is low, and the water near Ma Peng Bay is only a foot deep, making it impossible for cargo ships to pass up and down the river. More than 3,000 ships are stranded there, most of them carrying grain, with seafood, foreign goods, silk, satin, and wool accounting for about two-thirds. If no measures are taken to clear these stranded cargo ships, not only will the daily supply of rice for Shanghai be insufficient, but the shortage will also affect the circulation of money at the end of the year when the New Year is approaching. Moreover, the stranded goods may be subject to changes in market prices, spoilage of materials, or theft by shipowners. Such unexpected losses are inevitable. Currently, the only way to allow cargo ships to pass is to open the dams. Otherwise, the 3,000 cargo ships cannot fly to Shanghai. Not only will our grain merchants suffer this hardship, but all industries in Shanghai will also be affected. We urge you to forward this letter from the Grain Association to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting that the two departments of Jiangsu Civil Affairs and Construction allow the dams to be opened to release water to relieve commercial transportation and provide funds for circulation. It is reported that the goods and cargo previously stranded were worth about five to six million yuan, and were related to the cargo funds of various industries in Shanghai, such as grain, miscellaneous goods, seafood, foreign goods, silk, satin, and wool. Now, due to the shallow water in the Yunhe River, the goods are stranded, which is tantamount to stranding five to six million yuan of funds. At this time when the end of the year is approaching and funds are extremely tight, how will we raise funds for circulation? If we do not urgently take measures to open the river and allow passage, the more cargo ships gather, the more difficult it will be to circulate funds, and how will the cargo merchants survive this New Year? Therefore, we are informing you of the situation and respectfully request that you forward this letter to the two departments of Jiangsu Civil Affairs and Construction, urging them to open the dams immediately to allow the huge amount of stranded goods to pass, so as to relieve the commercial difficulties. We sincerely appreciate your public spirit.' Another newspaper report stated that representatives of the people in northern Jiangsu believed that the 10,000 boatmen were living in danger due to the stagnation of water and requested an announcement to all sectors of society. I deeply feel that with the end of the year approaching, if the river freezes, not only will the 10,000 boatmen be in dire straits, but the funds of Shanghai grain merchants and seafood, foreign goods, silk, satin, and wool industries will be even more difficult to circulate. We urgently inform you of the situation and enclose an advertisement, respectfully requesting your association to cable the Jiangsu Department of Construction to forward a telegram to the Northern Jiangsu Yunhe River Engineering Bureau to dredge the dams to create a lifeline and attach a newspaper advertisement from representatives of northern Jiangsu calling for signatures. Accordingly, the circulation of goods between Shanghai and various places in northern Jiangsu depends entirely on the Yunhe River. Now, due to the prolonged drought, the water near Ma Peng Bay is shallow, causing goods to be stranded. At the end of the year, when commercial funds are tight, the impact is indeed significant. It is now said that the only way to allow thousands of cargo ships to be transported is to dredge the dams. The competent authorities should promptly open the river to facilitate cargo transportation and relieve commercial difficulties.

Deeply appreciate your public spirit. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Shang Xian, bows."

Japanese Naval Landing Force Holds Field Combat Exercises

Atagoyama Arrives in the Yangtze River Yesterday

The more than seven hundred new recruits from the Japanese Ministry of the Navy who were transferred to Shanghai last month have been incorporated into four major teams by Commander Sugisaka and are undergoing intensified training. Yesterday at noon, Commander Sugisaka specially ordered the new soldiers to carry out field exercises, dividing the seven hundred new recruits into two major teams, one for attack and one for defense. Commander Sugisaka personally supervised, and Lieutenant Colonel Ohiso served as commander. They first held attack and defense operations in the eastern suburbs of Hongkou, first using infantry and then artillery. The exercise lasted about two hours. Afterwards, the defense team retreated to the vicinity of the Da Kang Textile Factory and practiced street fighting again. The sound of gunfire and artillery was frequent for a while, causing great panic among nearby residents. They returned to the team later. It is reported that a second large exercise will be held at the end of this month.

The flagship Atagoyama of the Japanese First Overseas Dispatch Force departed from Shanghai yesterday and headed to various ports along the Yangtze River to inspect the Japanese warships in various places. Commander Sakano took the ship to Wuhan.

Zhu Tieying Case Retried

Resembles Stealing Chickens with a Great Deal of Official Air

These Eight Characters Are Considered Insulting

Zhu Tieying, the editor of the Moye Bao in Taicang, was accused of satirizing Director Hu Jiacong in a report on business tax matters. County Magistrate Zhao Enju arrested Zhu and immediately sentenced him to one year in prison for harming the interests of the Republic of China, and fined him 100 yuan for failing to make corrections, and closed the newspaper. Zhu appealed to the Shanghai Local Court, arguing that the judgment was illegal. After several trials, the debate ended. It was now announced that the business tax had been exempted, so there was no harm to the interests of the Republic of China. However, the words "resembles stealing chickens with a great deal of official air" in the newspaper were close to scolding and insulting. Therefore, the judgment revoked the original judgment, but sentenced Zhu to three months in prison for publicly insulting a public official, and fined him 100 yuan for failing to make corrections in the newspaper. However, Zhu did not express his satisfaction after the judgment and may appeal to the third instance.

Since October, the import of Japanese goods has been extremely crowded. Recently, Japanese merchants heard that China and Russia have resumed diplomatic relations, and Russian goods will be sold to China. They are now rushing to ship goods to Shanghai. Yesterday, the Asamaru arrived, carrying more than 18,600 pieces of inferior goods, mainly including piece goods, machinery parts, yarn factory supplies, porcelain, and sugar. Compared to the crowded period, the load has increased by one-third. On the 19th, 20th, 24th, 27th, and 30th of this month, there will be five more large batches of inferior goods, about 60,000 to 70,000 pieces, arriving in Shanghai by the end of this month on the Mikasayama, Tsukuba Maru, Rokkosan Maru, and Maya Maru.

Knocking on Coffins to Ask for Flower Club Numbers

Their Stupidity is Incomparable

Flower Clubs Abound in Pudong

Recently, the practice of betting on flower clubs has become very popular in the coastal areas of Pudong. Ordinary people are addicted to this practice, and they often ask ghosts and gods for flower club numbers. The Bao An Corps and the police station separately cracked two cases the night before last and yesterday. 1) Liu Nianbao, a 25-year-old from Gaoyou, who lives at No. 159 Yangjiadu, works as a boatman. The night before last, he gathered his friends to burn incense and candles in the tombs behind the Yangjing Temple in Lan Nidu to knock on coffins for numbers. He was spotted by Bao An Corps member Yang Bingkui and others, who sent Liu and a lottery tube to the Third District Police Station for processing.

2) Xiao Jingfu, the patrol officer of the Third Section of the Third District of Tangqiao, saw that there were many gamblers in the territory. Yesterday, he led the police to arrest Du Deko, Zhu Guisheng, and Xiang Shicheng in the San Guan Tang area, and confiscated a lottery tube and several slips of paper. He took everything to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Selection Method for Chinese Real Estate Committee Members in the Public Concession

Each of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association and the Real Estate Association will select one person. On April 13 of this year, at the annual meeting of foreign ratepayers in the Public Concession, a proposal was passed, believing that two Chinese committee members should be added to the Real Estate Committee. The Municipal Council was authorized to contact representatives of the relevant countries in order to increase the number of Chinese committee members. At that time, the United States also expressed a hope that the interests of non-landlord Chinese ratepayers should be protected during the selection process. Subsequently, in July, the Municipal Council sent a letter to the Senior Consul, requesting that the proposal and hope be conveyed to the Diplomatic Corps and that Article 6A of the Public Concession Real Estate Regulations be revised to clearly protect the interests of Chinese ratepayers. Recently, Mayor Wu sent a letter to the Senior Consul, explaining the selection of these committee members. After considering this letter, the Municipal Council decided to waive the requirement for Municipal Council approval of the selected committee members. However, in order to realize the expectations of the annual ratepayers' meeting, one of the two Chinese committee members should be selected by the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, and this person should be neither a landlord nor a representative of a landlord. The other member should be selected by the Chinese Real Estate Association. Originally, there were three foreign real estate committee members in the Public Concession. One was appointed by the Municipal Council, one was elected by registered landlords (concurrently with the election of directors), and one was elected by the annual ratepayers' meeting. Now, with the addition of Chinese committee members, there will be a total of five real estate committee members. The Real Estate Committee has the power to adjudicate disputes arising from the Municipal Council's acquisition of land.

Zhu Jiheng Receives Swedish National Medal

The Swedish King bestows

Second Class Vasa Order

Mr. Zhu Jiheng, Secretary of the Swedish Consulate General in Shanghai, native of Wuxian, Bachelor of Political Science from St. John's University in Shanghai, assumed his current position in 1922 and has served for ten years. He is known for his diligence and conscientiousness and is highly regarded by successive consuls. He has a particularly close relationship with the current Consul General. It is now reported that the Swedish King has specially awarded him the Second Class Vasa Order to commend him. The Swedish Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai held a banquet at the Metropolitan Hotel on Sima Road the day before yesterday, where Acting Consul General Fei Shen personally presented the medal to Mr. Zhu, who received and wore it.

Success of Charity Ball

The Chinese Leprosy Relief Association held a charity ball at the Astor House Hotel last night. All proceeds from ticket sales will be used to subsidize the association's expenses. The enthusiastic participation of Chinese and Western ladies and gentlemen was unprecedented. After 9 o'clock, there was no space left on the dance floor. Prominent figures such as Zhang Gongquan, Huang Hanliang, and Wu Liande, and Yan Fuqing, all attended with their families. Li Yuanxin, Zhang Jiabu, Mrs. Xiao Zhiji, Wu Zhijian, Gao Sheqiang, Hua Junchao, Zhang Xianlun and others served as hosts. Lottery tickets were also sold on the spot, and all prizes were donated by individuals or companies. There were a total of 20 major prizes, which were drawn in public that evening. Zhang Gongquan and Schode were invited to supervise. The first prize, a Chinese painting personally painted by Mrs. Jiang Yiping, was won by a certain French gentleman. The second and third prizes were painted fans by Mrs. Jiang. The fourth prize was a suit from Henry Tailor. The fifth prize was a gold watch from Henry & Company. Among them, only the 12th prize number was 203, and the 14th prize number was 426, which have not yet been claimed. All other prizes have been claimed by the winners. The two winners who have not claimed their prizes can bring their tickets to the Chinese Leprosy Relief Association office at 20 Museum Road to claim them immediately.

Mechanic's Tragic Death

At approximately 8:25 yesterday morning at the Fuxin Seventh Flour Mill on Xinzha Grand Road, a mechanic named Huang Jianfu, 48 years old, from Ningbo, was accidentally crushed by machinery, losing his right shoulder and both legs. Blood gushed out like a spring, and he lost consciousness. He was then transported by the fire brigade to Renji Hospital for treatment but died at 9:30.

Old Woman Dies Tragically Next to Stove from Coal Poisoning

Arms and Legs Burned

Beware of Burning Coal Balls

The woman Mao Yin, 62 years old, residing at 32 Xinzha Road, whose son, Mao Ading, works at the waterworks, closed all the windows tightly in the pavilion loft due to her old age and fear of the cold, and burned coal balls in the stove to keep warm at around 6 PM the day before yesterday, while Ading had not yet returned home. Unexpectedly, she fainted from the gas in an instant, causing her to fall next to the stove. The clothes on her body were also burned by the fire, and her arms and legs were also burned. When her son returned home from work and knocked on the door without response, he managed to pry the door open and saw this situation. He quickly extinguished the fire, and fortunately, it was discovered early, so the house was not severely affected. He then transported his mother to Guangren Hospital for medical treatment, but due to the fire's toxins attacking her heart, she could not be saved and soon died. The hospital notified the Xinzha police station, who ordered detectives to investigate. The body was transported to the forensic examination office on Follen Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District District Court, arrived at the office to conduct an examination. He was informed by the deceased's son, Mao Ading, of the previous situation. Mr. Guo then pronounced that Mao Yin had died from burns sustained during her life, and the body was handed over to her son, Mao Ading, to prepare for burial.

Preliminary Announcement of Memorial Service for Ji Chuying

Mr. Ji Chuying traveled to Europe and America in his early years, united with comrades, and promoted revolution. After returning to China, he traveled north and south, working tirelessly. In recent years, he served at the Commercial Press and the National Central University, dedicating himself to writing and promoting culture, which was highly respected by prominent figures. During the January 28th Incident, Mr. Ji witnessed the tragic situation and became ill with sorrow and indignation, passing away last month. It is now reported that his close friends Wang Yunwu, Pan Xulun, Xu Peikun, and others have initiated a memorial service to be held at the Jade Buddha Temple on December 25. It is thought that Mr. Ji had extensive social connections during his lifetime, and it is expected that there will be a grand scene of mourning at that time.

Liangyou Photographic Group on the Northwest Journey

Recently Entered Shaanxi from Gansu

The Liangyou Photographic Travel Group, departing from Shanghai, has traveled for three months, covering over 20,000 li. They have collected a large number of photographs. The group has already worked in sections, initially along the Tianjin-Pukou Railway line, then explored various ports in East China by sea, visiting Shanhaiguan in the east and entering Tianjin. From there, they went to key areas in North China. At the beginning of November, they left Pingxi and traveled west, spending over forty days on the northwest journey. They photographed the Hetao area in great detail. Recently, they completed their work in Lanzhou and are heading to Xi'an via Pingliang. The Yellow River basin has been completed in stages. Except for slightly exceeding the budget, they have been fortunate to avoid unexpected difficulties and obstacles. The inconvenience of transportation and the hardships of traveling in the cold are all expected. Wherever the group goes, people in various places deeply appreciate this cultural initiative and are happy to support it.

Citizens of Nanjing Road Firmly Oppose Telephone Rate Hike

Refuting the Municipal Council's Reply

The Nanjing Road Business Association and the First District Branch of the Citizens' Association previously sent letters to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Ratepayers' Association, and others, requesting that they work together to oppose the telephone rate hike. Recently, they received a reply from the Municipal Council forwarded by these two associations. Dissatisfied with the reply, they sent another letter to the two associations yesterday, refuting the Municipal Council. The original letter stated: (To the Municipal Chamber of Commerce) In response to your letter of November 30, forwarding the Municipal Council's reply, which lists the Shanghai Telephone Company's losses over the years as justification for the telephone rate hike, we hereby reply that the Municipal Council published

Consultant for Readers

Mr. Wang Zhixin inquires: The difficulty of finding employment and the mismatch between education and employment are well-known facts in China today. Your publication has also discussed this issue several times, and I do not wish to express my opinions. Especially since I can be considered someone who has a job, even if it is somewhat "mismatched" and unsatisfactory. However, reading the news about people marching for hunger and demanding bread allows me to be content. But I want to raise a further question: how to maintain my job! To put it bluntly, how to "keep my rice bowl"? Because based on my feelings and observed facts, keeping one's rice bowl does not depend on ability but on connections and dog-like behavior. To put it nicely, it is called loyalty; more generally, it is called catering to and currying favor; to be blunt, it is called flattery! However, for me, these are precisely the most difficult conditions! I have no relatives, not even distant ones, to rely on, not even from the same hometown! My temperament is also somewhat eccentric, and I am not inclined to speak much, let alone engage in empty praise. The hypocritical and slavish nature of constantly saying "yes" is naturally something I cannot learn or imitate. But I don't want to lose my rice bowl. What should I do? To make a joke: should I introduce my younger female cousin to the manager? Or should I ask my wife to become a goddaughter? Otherwise, must I transform myself, put on a smiling face, and force myself to socialize? Here, I earnestly request your detailed guidance.

Reply: What you said in your letter is indeed true, and I believe it is not only you who feels this way. However, this is ultimately an abnormal state, not a normal one! In more modern and enlightened institutions, this problem has already been eliminated, and it is no longer as you describe in your letter. And the most important prerequisite should still be economic. Because the entire mode of production is still in a feudal stage, it is not surprising that there are such feudal blood ties and servility. Furthermore, there is the fear of unemployment. Because if not for that, things would not be this way. It is precisely because there are many job seekers that people prioritize relatives over outsiders, as the saying goes, "Arms do not bend outwards." Your publication previously published an article forcefully defending the company, which was subsequently refuted by our association. Now, the reasons cited by the Municipal Council still favor the company and are biased. It is truly outrageous. Although the telephone company has incurred huge expenses due to replacing old equipment with new ones, according to their own statement, from the company's establishment on August 5, 1930, to the end of September this year, a period of 26 months, the total loss amounted to 218,430 taels. Even considering the losses over 26 months, although the Shanghai Telephone Company has strived to expand its lines more than fourfold and has hired mostly Western staff, paying them generous salaries, it is a natural consequence of extravagance and miscalculation that they have incurred losses. This cannot serve as sufficient justification for a large price increase or for retroactively compensating for new prices. As it stands now, if you want to resolve the situation, quell the unrest, you must have accounting experts delegated by impartial social organizations audit the company's books to determine whether a price increase is justified and whether the amount of the increase is reasonable, in order to achieve a fair resolution. It is hoped that you will not be intimidated by pressure and willingly give up, sacrificing the interests of the majority. That would be fortunate. (To the Ratepayers' Association) In response to your letter of December 1 (the same as the letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, omitted), and noting that the association's letter to the Municipal Council on November 15 has not yet been replied to, we do not know why. We are also enclosing a draft of the letter to the Municipal Council for your reference (the letter to the Municipal Council has already been published in the newspaper on November 17 and is also omitted).

The teacher often writes "dry" or even "incoherent" on my papers. Sir, how can I avoid being dry, and how can I be coherent? The teacher has taught us to read more books. He has given us a very long reading list. When I saw that reading list, I initially felt flustered and didn't know which book to read. Later, although I bought a few books, I couldn't find any interest in them... Moreover, this method seems to take too long. Sir, do you have a better method?

Note: Even according to the reading list the teacher gave me, I personally don't have enough money to buy them all.

Reply: An article is generally inseparable from two parts: form and content. The so-called content is the essence of an article, the material it contains. Form is the tool for expressing this content. Having a tool of expression without anything to express is just an empty shell; this is "dryness." Having material but not knowing how to express it is "涩"; or if it is expressed but does not match the original intention, or if the tool of expression is used incorrectly, it is "incoherent." For example, a table: whether the tabletop is square or round, three-legged or four-legged, is the form. Whether it is made of pine, chestnut, or steel is the content. Drawing a table on paper, even if the form is complete, is empty and has no practical value; this is dryness. Just a pile of wood or steel is also not

Chinese Typewriter Company Donates Funds to Northeast Refugees

The China Industrial Company at No. 9 Hankou Road in Shanghai, recognizing that it is now the freezing winter in the borderlands, and the refugees in the three northeastern provinces are either wandering homeless, crying out to the heavens and earth, or sleeping in the open, suffering from hunger and cold, and the people in the rear cannot bear to sit idly by, are taking advantage of this Northeast Refugee Relief Entertainment Fair to donate to the refugees from the sale of the new Chinese typewriter, a completely domestic product patented by the National Government and produced by the company. The typewriter originally sold for 300 yuan, but now the company is selling it to customers at a 10% discount and will donate an additional 30 yuan to the Northeast refugees for each typewriter sold. This kind of righteous act is the first of its kind in the current industrial and commercial circles, and we hope that all circles will enthusiastically follow suit. It is said that a sample of the typewriter can be obtained for free from Mr. Yu Binqi of the Sports Group at the New World Entertainment Fair.

Shanghai County to Move its Governance, Effective January 1st

County Party Headquarters and Education Bureau to Move First

County Government and Finance Bureau to Follow

The issue of Shanghai County moving its seat of governance was submitted to the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Office for approval. The county government and construction bureau then created drawings and solicited bids for construction. Six months have passed since construction began, and the project has now been completed. The county government has scheduled to begin the move on January 1st. The details are recorded as follows:

New Site Completed

Since the establishment of the Shanghai Municipal Government, all areas under its jurisdiction have been incorporated into the urban area. This means that although the county government is located in the urban area, its administrative functions are primarily carried out in the surrounding rural towns. Therefore, the proposal to move the seat of governance was put forward. The county government then prepared a relocation plan, including drawings and budget, and submitted it to the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Office for approval. In June of this year, bids were solicited for construction at a cost of over 75,000 yuan. Since construction began, the project has progressed rapidly and is now fully completed.

Water and Electricity Supply

The new county seat is located in Beiqiao, which is traversed by the Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe Road. The area's commerce is quiet, and it is entirely a village. The county government's relocation here can realize Premier Sun Yat-sen's idea of "going to the people." The roads surrounding the new county government have also been fully paved. The electricity is supplied by a small generator installed by the Minhang Commercial Electric Light Company, providing electricity for the entire county government. In terms of drinking water, there is no tap water available in the area, making it inconvenient to install. Drilling artesian wells may also be too late, so the water from the Zhuye River in front of the new county government is currently used for drinking. The river flows east-west in front of the county government, connecting to the Beimiao Canal, and indirectly to the Huangpu River.

Convenient Transportation

The sides of the roads surrounding the county government are planted with trees for decoration, which has now been completed. As a result, the scenery is quite beautiful, and the air is particularly fresh. From Shanghai, long-distance buses on the Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe Road can reach the area. You can get off at Beiqiao Station, making transportation quite convenient.

Relocation Procedures

According to Ye Dezhen, secretary of the county government, speaking to a reporter from the Huadong News Agency, the new county government buildings have all been completed, and the decoration and painting are also nearing completion. Electric wires are now being installed, and electric lights are being installed. It is scheduled to relocate the county party headquarters and the Construction Bureau starting on New Year's Day next year, followed by the Education Bureau and the directly affiliated Public Security Branch of the county government. As for desks: this is astringent. If wood is made into tables, but not polished or painted, or it is neither square nor round, and if the four legs are fitted with three, it is also not practical; this is incomprehensible. We should choose good materials and make a decent and practical table; this is the true meaning of writing. The antidote for your "dry" or "incomprehensible" writing is "reading more," and there is no other "better way." The meaning of the three words "read more" is very important. First, you must know that what you are reading is indeed a "book," that is, a valuable book. The ones assigned by your teacher now are naturally valuable and worth reading. Second, you must truly "read" and not just flip through the book. Read it word by word, sentence by sentence, and look up or ask about anything you don't understand. When reading, you should always pay attention to the same meaning, and think about how you would write it yourself, and whether the author's expression is the best. When you encounter valuable ideas, your own insights, or beautiful phrases, you should immediately copy or mark them. Third, it must be "more" in substance, not just in number. Do it diligently, and there is no need to be "flustered." There is no such thing as a one-step path to success. "Getting rich quick" is the thought of a hopeless person. Everything that comes from hard work and perseverance is your own. I sympathize with your eagerness to improve, but if you find the method "too slow," you will inevitably fall into the trap of "more haste, less speed." As for the problem of buying books, you might consider organizing a book club, where everyone either contributes money to buy them together and takes turns reading them, and then gives them to the school library as a souvenir or draws lots to distribute them upon graduation; or each person buys several books and borrows them from each other, so that everyone can work together to solve the problem easily.

As for the county government and the Finance Bureau, because there are many files, they still need to be sorted and packed, so they will be relocated after the county party headquarters and the Education Bureau. By the end of January, all the relocation should be completed.

Building New Dormitories

For the convenience of office work during this relocation, a dormitory is specially built for the staff to live in. This dormitory is being built with separate funding and only started construction last month. It is expected to be completed in February.

Use of the Old Site

The existing county government site has been given to the municipal government. It is said that the municipal government plans to use it for the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Someone from the bureau came to inspect it a few days ago, but when the Public Security Bureau moves in the future, it will still need major repairs.

Power Outage in Nanshi Lasts Half an Hour

At 6:45 last night, the electricity suddenly went out in the area from Laoximen within the city of Nanshi to Xiaodongmen up to Laobeimen. Almost the entire Nanshi fell into darkness. Only the section west of Laobeimen maintained its original brightness. The power was restored after about half an hour. However, one thing was enough to make people wonder: when the lights went out, the entire Nanshi suddenly heard a very loud buzzing roar, similar to the venting sound when a train starts. At the time, some people suspected that this sound was related to the power outage, but even after the power was restored, the sound continued uninterrupted for a long time before subsiding. As for the reason for the sudden power outage, it is said that it was caused by the explosion of the generator's square shed.

Shooting of Soldier During "Lone Army" Filming in Shanghai

The Circumstances of the Accident Are Under Investigation

Actress Yang Liuqing Seriously Injured

"Lone Army," the debut film of the Shanghai Great China Film Company, is a war film. The first group of the film crew set off for Suzhou on the 5th, and the second group set off on the 15th. On the 16th, they officially started filming some of the war scenes. At about 7 a.m., Director Chen Fu led the entire cast and crew, along with a team of soldiers from the 87th Division stationed in Suzhou, to the filming location to prepare for filming a charge scene. Among the soldiers, someone mistakenly took a rifle loaded with live ammunition. Suddenly, bullets flew everywhere. One bullet hit Yang Liuqing, one of the actresses in the film, and killed a soldier named Wang Debiao. At the time, the wounded and the dead were immediately taken to the hospital, and a special telegram was sent to the Shanghai head office to discuss the aftermath. Yesterday morning, Zhang Peilan, the manager of the company, and Zhou Shidong, the production manager, took the early train to Suzhou to investigate the circumstances of the accident.

The Police Are Still Investigating Other Cases

The police lawyer Ru Baoyi stated that the defendants were carrying weapons and were specializing in robbing pedestrians of their property on various roads in the concession (commonly known as "peeling pigs"). The number of cases they have committed is countless. Yesterday, the defendants confessed to six robbery cases at the police station. However, according to the police investigation, they have actually committed more than ten robbery cases. Due to the limited time, it has not been possible to investigate in detail. It is requested that the defendants be detained pending further investigation and formal prosecution. After verifying the confession, Judge Qian briefly questioned the defendants and ordered them to be detained for further investigation and interrogation.

Meeting Minutes of the Family Industry Cooperative Factory

The Family Industry Cooperative Factory on the west side of Dihui Road in this city convened its first factory meeting yesterday (the 17th) at 2:00 p.m. More than 100 workers attended, and the Social Affairs Bureau sent Representative Tian to participate. Du Bingshou was publicly elected as the chairman at the time. He delivered an opening speech, followed by a speech by Representative Tian, who said that after the government promulgated the Factory Meeting Law, your factory is holding a meeting for the first time in accordance with the law, so the progress in the future can be used as a method by other factories. The purpose of holding this meeting is to seek cooperation between labor and management. The factory should be considerate of the workers' interests, and the workers should take care of the factory's business, so that labor-management disputes do not occur, which is not only beneficial to themselves but also beneficial to the country. Subsequently, workers' representatives were elected on the spot. Eight people were elected, one each from the makeup department, powder department, machine department, lithography department, and letterpress department, and three female worker representatives. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

Jin Learning Tide Blood

One Teacher and Student Mutually Mutilate

Student Military Police Clash Again

(Taiyuan Communication) The student tide in Taiyuan First Normal School caused a sensation. After the incident on the 22nd of last month, the perpetrators Du Lianxiu and Zhang Yaohua and other five students left the school without permission and did not return all night. After the school authorities found out, they decided to expel the five students. On the 24th, Yang Yuanrui and Li Changgeng led a total of 70 to 80 first-year students from the school to petition the Department of Education. They were not able to get their way, so they all returned to the school and stayed in the hall of the department for seven days. They were escorted back to the school by military police and gendarmes. It happened that the principal of the school, Huang, was detained by the procuratorate of the local court. No one in charge of the school, the petitioning students, returned in frustration and moved to the Wanzixiang Hotel. At 4:00 p.m. on the 7th of this month, led by Ma Ruilong and Li Danting, they attacked the school with bricks. At that time, roars echoed, and the arrogance was soaring. Tiles and gravel were thrown into the school, and many doors and windows were smashed. Five or six students in the school were hit in the head. The petitioning students, a total of six or seventy people, returned to their residences in frustration. At about 4:00 in the morning on the 20th, more than 300 students in the school were still dreaming sweetly. The petitioning students, a total of 40 or 50 people, led by Du Lianxiu, Zhang Yaohua, Yang Yuanrui, and Li Changgeng, returned to the school in a mixed formation. These students broke into the school, armed with knives and sticks, over the wall. The dormitories, faculty and staff dormitories, principal's office, grudges of students, self-study rooms, glass doors and windows, sundries, utensils, books, bedding, etc. of the school and affiliated primary school and vocational teachers were all smashed. The students in the school did not dare to stay. Wang Junying and others more than ten people were broken heads, broken legs, residual arms, blood spraying like springs, the situation is extremely pitiful. These students are now living in Shanxi Hospital for recuperation. According to the doctors, Wang and other three students suffered fatal injuries and are terrified of escaping. Liu Jun, the head of the affiliated primary school, and Liu Ying, a teacher training student, and other seven or eight people were tied up with hemp ropes and beaten with sticks by the petitioning students. Liu and others were seriously injured. When the reporter wrote this article, Liu and others had been bound for 16 hours. Liu and others were locked in a dark room of the school by the petitioning students, and the surveillance was very strict. It has not yet been heard that they will be released. The government, in the face of this tragedy, has once again staged a real tragedy, and is in pain and regret. It has decided to take effective measures in accordance with the previous order to solve the four principles of the school's storm. The order in the school is now maintained by military police and gendarmes sent by the authorities. The translation of the sports meeting, the petition letter of the tragedy, the division of the region, and the efforts to carry out affairs to determine the final male and female clouds, (12·13·Jiao Zhang in Taiyuan Hotel)

More than a thousand students from Jin Yishi, Chengzongyang Xing Nvshi Teacher's College Affiliated Middle School and other schools went to the provincial government to petition on the 17th. After the End of the Shandong Student Unrest

Middle School Graduate Joint Examination

Scheduled to be Held in Seven Locations

Jinan Dispatch: The Education Department, acting on instructions from the Ministry of Education, is organizing this year's winter joint examination for middle school graduates. An official order had already been issued to all schools. Senior high school students expressed their opposition, which led to a major disturbance. Senior high schools have been explicitly ordered to disband, and efforts are currently underway to manage the aftermath. The Education Department is continuing its work on this matter. The examination dates have been set for January 16th to 18th. (Graduation exams for all schools and classes must be completed before January 10th.) Examination locations have also been designated. In Jinan, schools will take the joint examination at the First Middle School, Girls' Middle School, Zheng Yi School, Yu Ying School, and Dongying, totaling five locations. The county middle schools of Gaomi, Shouguang, and Weixian will take the exam in Weixian. The provincial Eighth Middle School and Bushan Junior Middle School will take the exam in Yantai. The provincial Fifth Middle School will take the exam in Linyi. The provincial Eleventh Middle School will take the exam in Linqing. The Wudeng County Junior Middle School will take the exam in Wudeng, and the Huangxian County Junior Middle School will take the exam in Huangxian. Today (the 15th), the Education Department, in accordance with the above-mentioned locations and dates, issued an order to all provincial, county, and private middle schools in the province to comply. On one hand, they are actively organizing the Joint Examination Committee, which will be established soon, to handle the joint examination matters in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Education.
