Special Article

Speaking Out for Middle Schools Nationwide (3)

— Liao Maoru

We do not support the cancellation of the division between arts and sciences, not because we undervalue mathematics and science. The key to building a solid foundation in mathematics and science is to provide rigorous training to junior high school students. If the mathematics and science courses in junior high school are taught well, students with a slight aptitude for mathematics and science will naturally pursue that path. Even for students with less talent, if you lighten the teaching materials and teach them slowly, they can still keep up. This is the way to cater to individual needs and abilities. How can it be done otherwise?

Let's not talk about our own country for now; let's see what the situation is like in foreign countries. The division of subjects in middle school can be said to be a common phenomenon in various countries. However, in the United States, many courses are divided within the same school. In European countries, many courses are divided within schools of the same level to meet individual needs. Although the methods differ, the principles are the same. For example, Germany has humanities middle schools, practical science middle schools, and science middle schools, similar to the four types of middle schools recently proposed. The curricula are also different, with some focusing on ancient culture, some on the comparative culture of various European countries, some on mathematics and science, and some on the entirety of German culture. Since middle school subjects are too numerous and varied, it is impossible to cover everything in detail. Dividing them into several courses can allow each school to have a central purpose. France, known for its conservatism, has fierce debates about middle school curricula. However, the 1902 education system divided the early middle school into two types of courses, A and B. Type A focused on classical literature, and Type B focused on modern literature and science. The later stage was divided into four types of courses, making the distinction between arts and sciences even clearer. In 1923, although the government had a tendency to return to the classics, ordering all middle schools to study the same courses for the first four years, the second phase was divided into three branches, with arts and sciences still clearly separated. This return to tradition was opposed by various parties, and in 1925, the government revised it, dividing the first four and last two years of middle school into two groups, A and B, balancing the benefits of liberal arts education and practical education, and reconciling student interests with the postponement of specialization. The British education system is the most complex, but the British advocate freedom, so there are many different types of schools to meet the special needs of young people. The most fixed and uniform system is that of Japan. Some say that the curriculum promulgated by the government this time is largely influenced by Japanese middle schools. However, Japanese middle schools are nominally five years, but in reality, only four. Many middle school students who have completed four years of study apply to higher schools, so the current middle school has become a disguised junior high school, while higher schools are equivalent to high schools. Although middle schools do not divide subjects, higher schools do, and the Japanese education system, with primary schools and middle schools running parallel, also uses many different types of schools to meet the needs of different students. This is similar to the European education system. After our country canceled the division of subjects in ordinary middle schools, there are no other schools to remedy the situation, which is very different from Japan.

Another point we must know is that Japan is very serious about education and is not willing to change it easily. Their middle school curriculum has been preserved to this day after many years of experimentation and improvement. They have not rashly adopted any one system. I remember that when the author visited Japan for the second time, the Ministry of Education was studying the teaching methods of English classes in middle schools. They started with phonetics, invited experts to guide them, and designated one or two middle schools to be responsible for testing. After the test had achieved results, they would then order all middle schools in the country to follow suit. Their government requires so much effort for even a partial issue of middle school teaching methods. As for the entire curriculum, how could they suddenly order all schools in the country to change it without a long period of research and testing? Once, Wen Kang asked Zhong Hui, "What did you hear to come, and what did you see to leave?" We should also ask the Ministry of Education why the provisional standards of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China were suddenly promulgated and suddenly canceled. What were the results of the experiment? What were the advantages and disadvantages? Will the new curriculum be overturned again after being implemented for a year or six months? Education is a major national matter, and such easy changes are disappointing.

3. Canceling the Credit System and Elective System is Too Rigid

When the credit system and elective system were first implemented, there may have been drawbacks, such as: (1) Courses were scattered and unsystematic; (2) Students had no standards for choosing courses; (3) Major subjects might be lowered. However, after more than ten years of improvement, these problems have been largely resolved. Now, suddenly restoring the old system and wiping out more than ten years of hard work does not seem like the administrative authorities are encouraging schools to move forward. We often hear people say that China's education has gone bankrupt, and that the level of Chinese students is declining year by year. Whether education has gone bankrupt and whether the level of students is declining year by year has no objective evidence. Even if it is true, we should investigate the real reasons and try to remedy them, not just echo the sentiments and blame everything on the credit system and elective system. After the September 18th Incident last year, few students across the country could concentrate on their studies, which led to difficulties in applying to universities this summer. Can we blame the elective system and credit system for this? National politics are turbulent, the economy is declining, and administrative authorities and social elites cannot set an example for young people, which leads to successive student movements and a decline in academic atmosphere. Can we blame the elective system and credit system for this? The United States and various European countries all have elective systems. Why don't we hear them protesting? "Our country has a vast territory, and the conditions in various places are different" (see the Ministry of Education's circular). Don't say that the fixed curriculum now promulgated by the Ministry of Education cannot suit the conditions of various places and the needs of various schools; even after decades or centuries, enlightened educational administrative authorities should not hold this idea. The Ministry of Education can only stipulate the general outline and must leave room for flexibility. We must know that there are many courses that can be offered in middle schools, and the Ministry of Education can never list all the important subjects in the curriculum. The subjects listed in the curriculum are not necessarily the most important, and the allocation of time may not be appropriate. To give an example, the curriculum promulgated this time lists drawing as a compulsory subject in high school and has two hours per week. If high school students study drawing for two hours every week, and everyone becomes an artist, that would be great. However, artistic talent cannot be forced. Rather than teaching most young people to scribble meaninglessly, why not offer several elective courses and let them choose to study according to their interests? Therefore, canceling the credit system and elective system only has disadvantages, and we cannot see any benefits.

Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Faculty and Staff Temporary Congress of Full Representatives

Petitioning the Education Fee Management Office to Issue Salaries

Director Niu is Responsible for Issuing Two and a Half Months of Funding

Consulting on Concrete Measures Last Night, Another Meeting Today

The Jiangsu Provincial United Association of Middle School Faculty and Staff held a temporary congress of full representatives at 10:00 AM on the 16th at the Second Academy of Nanjing Middle School. The proceedings of the meeting are recorded below.

Attending Representatives

Song Zhongjiang Chen Cheng, Su Girls' Normal School Yang Guangjun, Yang Zhong Wu Cangli Wang Xiaoshang Yin Mingfu, Hai Normal School Zhang Jingfeng, Su Agriculture Zhu Yuqing, Shang Zhong Chen Yue Wen Xuancheng, Taicang Normal School Zhang Yuanming Xie Fanghui, Hushuguan Party School Jiang Cuiying Zhou Yisong, Girls' Middle School Zhang Huiheng, Party Normal School Wu Dezhang Wang Weiyi Xia Peiri, Luoshe Township Normal School Gao Hongqi, Jieshou Township Normal School Wang Zhenhua, Nan Zhong Zhou Zhongchen Zhou Yueren, Guanyun Township Normal School Xu Yisheng, Rugao Normal School Feng Mingfu, Su Ding Wu Xuepei, Chang Zhong Wu Xuezeng Wu Zhipu, Tong Zhong Cheng Jifang, Huangdu Township Normal School Geng Qinghua, Xi Normal School Zhang Zhongyou Gao Yizhi, Xu Zhong Xu Yinkun, Nan Girls' Middle School Tian Muzhi, Yan Zhong Qiao Yuhong, Xu Girls' Normal School Mao Shuda, Wujiang Township Normal School Zhu Wenda, Su Zhong Zhang Gongsu Chen Yongfeng, etc., totaling 26 schools and 37 representatives.

Morning Meeting

The meeting began at 10:00 AM with due ceremony. First, Wu Dezhang, a Standing Committee member of the Executive Committee, reported on the purpose and process of convening this temporary congress. Then, he introduced the newly joined Rural Normal School members. Wu Dezhang was publicly elected as the chairman of today's meeting, and Chen Yue was the secretary. Liu Beihe, Section Chief of the Education Fee Management Office, attended the meeting upon invitation and reported that Section Chief Yang Zishen of the office was currently urging various counties to pay up and would return to Nanjing tomorrow, at which point the amount of education fees collected this time would be known. The Management Office has already completely issued notifications for the first half of August's funding for provincial schools. Part of the funds was temporarily advanced after negotiating with the bank. The notification for the second half of August's funding was already filled out, but has not been issued because the funds are still insufficient. After Liu's report, the faculty and staff representatives earnestly expressed the difficult situation of the accumulated arrears of funding for provincial schools, hoping that the Management Office would be truly responsible for issuing the accumulated arrears. It happened that Director Niu had a phone call and summoned Section Chief Liu back to the office, so he entrusted Liu to arrange for all representatives to go to the Management Office at 3:00 PM today to meet with Director Niu in person. Then, the minimum standard for requesting funding was discussed. It was decided that the minimum standard was to issue the funding for August, September, and October (a total of two and a half months, including the half month already issued in August) and to have a concrete guarantee. (Rural Normal Schools that have already issued more funding than other middle schools in advance will still be handled according to the old plan.) The representatives unanimously agreed that the so-called issuing three months (that is, two and a half months) refers to the present situation, and they still hope to issue the funding for November before the winter vacation. Then, the proposal to express opinions on the unsuitable and unrealistic situation of the Measures for Service and Treatment of Faculty and Staff of Secondary Schools promulgated by the Ministry of Education was discussed. The five resolutions passed by the Executive Committee in the last two meetings were submitted for discussion. Only the third item on salary was slightly changed, and the rest were passed as is. (1) Implement a full-time teacher system, and do not calculate salaries by the hour. (2) Teaching hours: 14 to 18 hours per week for high school, 16 to 20 hours per week for junior high school. (3) Salaries: 140 to 200 yuan per month for high school, 100 to 150 yuan per month for junior high school. (4) The actual budget should be calculated using the median of the teaching hours and the median of the salaries. (5) Those who hold grade or department positions should reduce teaching time by six hours. Then, Zhang Gongsu of Su Zhong, Zhou Yueren of Nan Zhong, Xia Peibai of Zhen Normal School, Wu Cangli of Yang Zhong, Wen Xuancheng of Shang Zhong, Zhu Wenda of Wujiang Township Normal School, and Zhang Zhongyou of Xi Normal School were publicly elected as representatives of the seven schools to go to the Ministry of Education tomorrow to petition and state the above opinions. At 1:00 PM, lunch was served, and in the afternoon, all representatives took a photo.

Afternoon Petition

At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, more than 30 representatives went to the Education Fee Management Office. It happened that Director Niu had important official business at the Ministry of Civil Service Affairs and did not arrive until 4:00 PM. Wu Dezhang, Zhang Zhongyou, Zhang Gongsu, Xia Peibai, Wang Xiaoshang, and Chen Yue, the representatives of the faculty and staff, successively expressed their opinions based on the resolutions. Section Chief Liu Beihe reported that he had recently telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, stating that the provincial schools' funding was in arrears for four months, and that the schools were eagerly awaiting funding for the upcoming year-end holidays. He requested that the 365,000 yuan owed to the province for the nineteenth and twentieth years of the Republic of China be repaid. (The provincial funds were to be subsidized 300,000 yuan each year. 65,000 yuan was owed in the nineteenth year, and nothing was paid in the twentieth year, totaling the above amount. This 300,000 yuan subsidy had been approved by the provincial government and included in the official budget. In the twenty-first year, the Department of Finance was unwilling to subsidize, and the Department of Education strongly argued for it, resulting in a compromise. Therefore, whether or not the subsidy will be paid in the twenty-first year is still uncertain. However, the old debts of the nineteenth and twentieth years should be paid.) It was requested that half of the amount be allocated in the middle of this month to meet urgent needs, and the Department of Education was also telegraphed to negotiate with the Department of Finance to raise funds as much as possible. Currently, the Department of Education has only telegraphed back saying that the Department of Finance has agreed to allocate a portion (it is not known how much). As for the Management Office directly ordering various county bureaus, they were limited to clearing the October education fees by the 15th of this month and clearing the November funding by the 25th, and Yang Zishen was sent to various counties to urge them, etc. Director Niu Tisheng said that it was too much to say that the faculty and staff had only received the salary for the first half of August, half a month since the provincial schools started. He had already thought of many ways. 1. Ask the Department of Finance to raise half of the outstanding subsidies first. 2. Organize and urge the payment of arrears from various counties. 3. Consider borrowing money. At this time of harvest, it is the peak season, and it is estimated that, with the combined efforts of all parties, in addition to the notification for the second half of August, which has already been filled out and is awaiting funding, the September notification can be signed and issued by the Audit Committee on the 25th of this month, and the October notification can be signed and issued by the Audit Committee on January 10th. The Management Office can be responsible for issuing these two and a half months (that is, August, September, and October) of funding. As for the hope of the provincial school colleagues to issue the November funding, the Management Office will do its best. By January 30th, perhaps one month or half a month of November can still be issued. In general, they will try their best to meet everyone's hopes. The representatives were very satisfied with Director Niu's sincere attitude and with the efforts of Section Chief Yang to urge payment. Director Niu arranged for the representatives to meet again at the Management Office at 7:00 PM on the 17th to discuss concrete measures and to learn about the latest education fees received by Section Chief Yang. The meeting then adjourned, and the representatives went to the banquet hosted by Principal Zhang of Nan Zhong. The representatives decided to meet again at 10:00 AM on the 17th to prepare the seven representatives to go to the Ministry of Education to petition.

Shanghai Education Bureau Revises the Judging Standards for Primary and Secondary School Health Competitions

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday instructed municipal and registered private primary and secondary schools, stating that in order to enhance students' health knowledge and train students' speaking skills, the bureau had previously decided to hold health speaking competitions for primary and secondary schools and had issued rules for all schools to follow. All judging standards were also stipulated in the rules. Now, the bureau has decided to revise these standards slightly at the 250th bureau affairs meeting. In addition to the judges following the revised standards, the revised standards are copied and issued for your information. This order includes a copy of the revised judging standards for primary and secondary school health speaking competitions. (1) Content, ideas, structure: 40%. (2) Language (tone, wording): 35%. (3) Posture: 25%.

The Municipal Education Bureau Cracks Down on Schools Using False Names for Deception

The Municipal Education Bureau previously found an advertisement in the November 10th Xinwen Bao advertising column for the Moonlight English School at 474 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, offering "Sex History" with an image of the author Zhang Jingsheng. The bureau immediately sent personnel to investigate and found that there was no Moonlight English School at that address. There was only a general affairs office located in the Lianyi Trading Company behind Shi Weiji on Nanjing Road, which was the place to sell the books mentioned in the advertisement. The bureau believes that it is using the name of the school to publish advertisements and deceive people. It has already sent a letter to the First Special District Local Court to strictly crack down on it to serve as a warning and avoid being fooled.

The Municipal Education Bureau Schedules Examinations for Primary School Teachers

The registration for the second session of the examination for primary school teachers organized by the Municipal Education Bureau has already begun. Therefore, many people have been enthusiastically requesting application forms in recent days. The bureau has scheduled physical examinations at the bureau on the 22nd of this month, and the registration deadline will also be at that time. Oral and written examinations will be held at Wuben Girls' Middle School on the 25th. In order to focus on the qualifications of primary school teachers, the bureau, in addition to already reorganizing the teaching staff of municipal schools, will also order private schools from the next semester onwards not to hire unqualified teachers. Teachers whose examination validity has expired or who have not registered due to a lack of registration qualifications should register as soon as possible to wait for the examination.

Jinan Again Defeats Donghua

Donghua's Feng Yunyou and Li Ning Injured

Jinan's Walk-off Resumption Sparks Penalty Kick Controversy

Donghua and Jinan met at the baseball field yesterday for the Western League Group A match. Jinan came back from behind to win 3-2. In the middle, Jinan left the field for several minutes due to a penalty kick. They were eventually persuaded to return to the field and resume the game, which was a stroke of great fortune. The referee was Bratland.

Jinan Team

Liu Zukan

Gu Shangdong Liang Shutang Chen Zhenhe

Xie Quanhe Zhuang Shihong Xu Yahui

Jiang Shanjing Chen Zhenxiang Zhang Hongzao

Mei Hongbao

Wan Xianghua

Li Ning Chen Pu Chen Hongguang

Zhou Xianyan Feng Yunyou Li Yichen

Guan Zhuanan Tu Kaiyuan Chen Jiaqiu

Referee's Interference Causes Dispute

Donghua and Jinan have equal talent, and the reunion of strong teams is sure to be exciting. At the beginning of the game, they met with courtesy, and the audience was pleasantly surprised, thinking that everything would be fine. However, after thirty minutes, Jiang Shan and Jing Li Yichen clashed in the penalty area. The referee interfered and bounced the ball on the ground again at the penalty spot. The figures were chaotic, and Chen Zhenhe pointed and crashed into the penalty kick. The entire Jinan team left the field and was persuaded to return, but had already lost two goals. After that, their actions were dominated by anger and they were unable to control themselves, which was regrettable.

Why Be Crude When the Performance is Exquisite?

Donghua's opening was smooth and continuous, with a very good appearance. The first thirty minutes of the first half were even more dazzling. Later, due to pressure from the opposing rules, they retreated to avoid injury, so there was little performance. In the second half, Donghua's fortunes turned. Feng Yunyou became dizzy and left the field, and Li Ning fought back with an injury, amidst all kinds of difficulties, not knowing where to go. At that time, Jinan had the entire field, and both offense and defense were fierce. If they could have acted civilly, it would have been a truly satisfying performance. Why was it that they could not restrain their wild nature and committed many fouls? Although they won the final victory, it was still felt to be imperfect.

A Huge Gust of Wind Sweeps into the Goal

Donghua gained momentum with the help of the wind and took the lead in the attack, taking advantage of the free kick to pounce into the formation. Jiang Shanjing's save became a corner kick. Cao Qiuting kicked it well, and Chen Hongguang volleyed it towards the goal. Xie Quanhe had anticipated this and calmly escaped the danger. Jinan's Chen Zhenhe came head-on, and the Donghua line shook. Zhou Xianyan personally came out to calm the storm. Jinan was pressured again, and Wan Xianghua's attack failed, turning into a corner kick. The kick was made into the field, and Chen Hongguang once again entered Wan's, shooting towards the goal. A huge gust of wind swept into the goal. Such a spectacle stunned the entire audience.

Penalty Kick Causes Trouble from Then On

Jinan, facing the sun and wind, was naturally in a defensive position. Captain Chen's spirit moved, and he changed the line to strengthen the internal strength. The brothers exchanged positions. At this time, Wan Xianghua suddenly attacked with lightning speed, missing by an inch. Otherwise, it would have been dangerous. Afterwards, Jinan rushed into the empty city, the ball moved from left to right, and Mei Hongbao raised his foot to take the penalty kick. Zhou Xianyan fell to the ground to stop him, and the ball turned against him. Then, the Jiang Li clash occurred in Jinan's penalty area, followed by a penalty kick. Jinan left and re-entered the field, losing the second goal. The peaceful world caused trouble from then on. Not five minutes later, Mei Hongbao received a ball from Chen and passed it to the left. At that time, Zhou Xianyan and Li Ning gathered together, and the left was empty. The new general Zhang Hongzao met a header and fell into the goal. Before long, the first half ended, with Donghua leading 2-1.

Two Goals in a Row Lead to Donghua's Failure

The two teams changed sides to fight again. The situation was different, and the situation changed. Although Jinan was trailing 1-2, they were full of vigor. They began to attack fiercely, sparing no effort. Donghua's forwards retreated to avoid damage. Only Wan Xianghua dared to venture into the unknown. Li Yichen occasionally got the ball and was trapped in the formation, with no way to find. Returning to Donghua, Zhou Xianyan rolled on the ground and threw it out, with continuous surprises and waves. Li Ning was injured and left the field, resting and returning, but his strength was greatly reduced. Soon Feng Yunyou left the field dizzy, and the interior shook. Chen Zhenhe changed to forward and launched a major attack. Zhou Xianyan fell to the ground to save the ball, Zhang Hongzao rushed to kick it into the goal, creating a draw. Not two minutes later, Li Yichen kicked a free kick, 20 yards from the goal, and took the gate directly. Hitting the post and bouncing back, Chen Hongguang continued to shoot, and Xie caught it with both hands. Jinan's entire army came again. Zhou Xianyan was too eager to save, and was too far from the barrier. Mei kicked it, wanting to return but it was too late, and failed 2-3. Afterwards, Donghua was still trying to find a way out in the encirclement, but it was difficult to add to their favor. As a result, in the Western League Group A match, Donghua suffered its first defeat 2-3.

Unfortunate Events Are Seen Again

Before the game, Jinan coach Yu Hengzhi, in the spirit of friendship, invited players from both sides to open their hearts and minds. All the previous events were considered dead, and he hoped to rebuild friendship. However, due to the referee's interference, friction arose, and Jinan's departure from the field gave outsiders a bad impression. Furthermore, the actions were often crude and inappropriate. In short, yesterday's unfortunate events were, to some extent, due to the referee's excessive nitpicking, which was not without reason. The result of the game is undoubtedly valid, but whether the future outcome will be affected will depend on the decision of the Westerners Association Executive Committee.

A Study of Football Tactics (3)

Written in Response to the First Defeat of the Ba City Qunli Team

Anyone with a basic understanding of football knows that the success or failure of a team depends on the entire team's ability to cooperate. Individual performances are detrimental and useless. A single stick is easily broken, but a bundle is hard to destroy. This theory is an ancient truth. The rainbow team members are the main characters in combining a team. Only by uniting the majority of individuals can a complete whole be produced. I believe that if the whole is to improve, it is necessary to start with the individual aspects first. Because if the individual measures are proficient, it will be easier to create small parts of contact. From the understanding of the small parts, the entire cooperation function can be further created. Otherwise, if the individual does not have the instinct to control the ball and the wisdom of the competition, even if you have a clear idea of the overall plan and a wonderfully arranged battle, you will be unable to implement it and ultimately fail. Therefore, if Qunli wants to improve the entire team in the future, it must first seek progress from the players' side. It is a pity that personal progress cannot achieve miraculous results overnight. We still have many upcoming championship games in the near future. We must have a step-by-step approach to temporarily cope with the situation, and then gradually seek fundamental treatment and improvement.

Ali Fei used the middle road blocking defense method to control us and build a great achievement. Then, I believe that other teams will follow suit and use the same tactics and formations to deal with Qunli. Therefore, we must prepare early and not repeat the mistakes of the past. The next time this situation occurs, we must use the lure-the-enemy-out-of-position method and the scattered attack method, developing from both wings to break the enemy. If the enemy still wants to monitor me and Ya Dai in the same way, then let them monitor us. The best way is for other teammates to find ways to attack from both sides, completely forgetting about me and Ya Dai. Don't always think about passing the ball to us. This Temporary Starvation method is used to disrupt the enemy and deceive their minds. Once the enemy's defenses are slightly relaxed, they should find an opportunity to unexpectedly pass the ball to us, which will be easier to succeed. If the enemy refuses to disperse or loosen their grip, then me and Ya Dai have no choice but to do our part, and the rest must find ways to win. In this way, we should take full advantage, because the enemy must have more than two people to monitor us, which is useless. If the enemy uses three people to monitor us two, counting the deduction, each team has eleven people, aren't our nine people fighting his eight people? With the strength of nine people, even if the one-on-one strength is average, it is reasonable to defeat the eight people. In addition, the center-back line is the key to the team's advance and retreat, and the attack and defense are crucial. Success or failure depends on it. Therefore, the center-back line must not be too far away from the forwards. When the forwards attack, they must move forward with them, working from the encirclement to intercept and attack again when the enemy's defense clears. At the same time, the defenders must also be cautious to avoid the disadvantage of not being able to respond from the front and the rear. (If everyone has a good memory, they should remember the first time Lehua went south. At that time, weren't we also often blocked by the majority of the central road advance? At that time, weren't Lehua's two wings the same as the current Qunli team, with mediocre talents? But Lehua's ability to fight and win was all due to the power of the center-back line assisting in the attack. The strength of the center-back line is inextricably linked to a team's strength). In addition, our Long Swinging Passing and FirstTimePassing are lacking. (Qunli's close combat and communication are passable, but long-range attacks are easier. A team must have both methods to be foolproof. We often see them use broadswords to charge into battle like South China). Kicking the ball also often makes the mistake of being too high and too far. Too high takes time and is difficult to accept (very few top-notch teams kick the ball more than ten feet high. I have seen it in Czech teams. The speed of the ball back and forth is twice as fast as here). Too far makes the forwards run in vain. OverkickingMeansOverrunningyourOwnForwards Both are inappropriate. Everyone work hard to improve. If we implement the steps mentioned above, although I dare not guarantee that we will always win in the future, I can guarantee that we will have a better and more disciplined performance than before, which will be noticed by the audience.

Commercial News

Peaceful Gold Market

(Trading in a weak market)

According to foreign telegraphs this morning, London's gold price slightly decreased. American silver remained unchanged. The exchange rate between Britain and America remained high. There was no significant change in forward silver prices or American cotton. The gold market opened slightly lower at 807.2 taels. Afterwards, foreign exchange rates were announced. The British exchange rate for this month was 1 shilling 8 pence 125, and the American exchange rate was 27.6875 yuan, slightly tighter than the previous day's closing price. Dadecheng's purchase immediately rose from 7 taels to 7.5 taels. Huabi ate up March American gold at 0.0625. Tianfeng Yongwanxing and others came on the market to compete for purchase, reaching 0.088 taels. Later, Hengxing came up to sell and Hengyu also came out, so it retreated to 6.2 taels. Retail investors bought a little at 7.6 taels. When HSBC announced its price at 9:30, the shilling remained unchanged. Due to the exchange rate squeeze, the American gold was lengthened by 25, falling to around 6 taels. However, the banks' appetite was still good. Huabi settled in January American gold at 875. Hengyu Dadecheng came on the market to buy, and there were no wholesale transactions in the market. The price hovered between 7 and 8 taels for a long time. Near 10:30, Hengxing came on the market to continue selling, and Zhaofengchang and others sold as well, dropping to 4.6 taels. However, the banks' appetite remained good, and the gold price was pulled up. Fuxing Yongyi Yilai bought, rising to 5.9 taels. Afterwards, with the ebb and flow of retail investors, it lingered between 5 and 6 taels. Finally, people's confidence revived, because Zhongfu entered January American gold at 27.875 yuan and Citibank ate February at 28 yuan. The buying sentiment in the market was strong again. Yuanmao Yongfu Yu competed to enter, so it was raised to 7.1 taels at the close. The goods were auctioned at 6.7 taels. The market is closed this afternoon due to Saturday.

Decline of 1.3 Taels

According to the city's highest price of 808.8 taels and the lowest price of 0.046 taels, there was a fluctuation of more than 4 taels, slightly lower than the previous day's closing price by 1.3 taels.

Opening Price Reduced by 7 Taels

The raised price was 873 taels with American gold at 0.25 yuan, a reduction of 66-67 taels. Later, it was 65 taels to 68 taels, and finally 66 taels, 7 taels less than the previous day. The December registration was 808 taels. January and February were both 807 taels, and the water supplement was 805 taels.

Not Much Trading in Each Firm

According to statistics, the trading on the table varied greatly between supply and demand. Hengchang Yong, Zhaofengchang, Qianchangxiang, Yongfeng, Fuxingyong, Yifengyong, Zhifengyongfu Taiheng, goods, etc. were buyers. Wanxing, Shunli, Yuanheng, Runchangyu, Yuanmao Yong, and Yuhe were all sellers. Hengyu and Fuyu sometimes came out and sometimes entered. Dadecheng entered more and exited less. Daxingyong and Changshengyong exited and then entered. The Dalian gang sold a total of 4-500 bars and only entered about 200. Hengxing, on behalf of the Guangdong gang, sold more than 1,000 bars. The amount of two-month bars in each firm totaled more than 18,000 on the first day on the market before yesterday, it was said.

Cooked Red Added 8.5 Taels

Yesterday, the cooked red price was still increased by 8.5 taels. There was not much trading. It is estimated that Yang Qinghe, Fuji, and Qiu Tianbao sold a total of about 300 taels to Yingfeng Hengtongfeng Yong, etc.

More Than 4,000 Not Yet Settled

All December to January bid gold swaps, the short side Hengxing swapped to Yingfeng Heng, and the long side paid 5 qian due to the small cooked red price (if the cooked red price is increased by 10 taels, the swap can be settled). January to February were generally settled, and among them, 7 bars were traded at a price of 2 qian paid by the long side. In general, the bulls were only willing to settle at the same price, while the shorts wanted to increase their current stock, so there were still more than 4,000 that had not been settled.

The Process During the Week Was Very Good

It is found that the market situation this week has rebounded and soared, but the changes have been very dramatic. In January, the smallest price at the beginning of the week was 796.6 taels. On Friday (the 16th), the swap happened to be held, but the prices for the two months were the same. The largest price ever reached an unprecedented high of 819.8 taels. The total review of 23.2 taels in January showed that the 1-2 month swap price was leveled, an increase of 7.4 taels compared to last Saturday.

Exchange Market British Tight and American Loose

Yesterday's silver market was still characterized by British shrinkage (which has been falling for a week) and American stability. Private telegraphs were not updated, and forward prices rose slightly by 1 hao. The exchange rate also rose for 6-7 days, rising by 2.375 to 8125 yesterday. As for the Shanghai market, the exchange rate was slightly different. The HSBC-listed American gold was lengthened by 25, and other currencies such as French and German also followed. British, Indian, Hong Kong, and Singapore currencies remained unchanged. This was probably because the domestic market was also related to the exchange rate, so the British market was tight and the American market was loose. It is estimated that British gold initially rose steadily and then leveled off, and finally shrank by 0.0625 compared to the previous day. American gold was stable in the morning, then loosened, and recovered to stability at noon. The overall increase was slightly 0.0625. The trading volume of each bank was not quiet. It is estimated that there were more than 100,000 pounds of British gold, and each firm mostly sold it off. Bombay electricity entered January, and American gold was sold by the gold industry again for 4-500,000 yuan. Banks such as Huabi and old Citibank continued to absorb it. American Bank bought March, and the market was closed on Saturday.

The Weekend Financial Market Remains Quiet

Yesterday was Saturday, and the atmosphere in the money and banking sector was typically quiet. Although foreign exchange was not deserted, transactions in silver dollars and foreign funds were sluggish. Only banknotes, due to a need in Hankou estimated at two to three million, saw active buying and selling in the market and frantic searches by banks. The situation with silver funds and subsidiary currency remained unchanged. Copper coins showed a slight increase, but mostly hovered around the same level.

(Fixed Exchange Rate, Slight Silver Discount) The "foreign exchange rate" remained unchanged from the previous day's afternoon market at 7 mace, 1 fen, and 4 li in both the morning and afternoon sessions. Competition was intense, but buying and selling forces were evenly matched, resulting in a stable situation. The "silver discount" opened at 2 fen in both the morning and afternoon sessions, remaining steady. However, it briefly reached 2.3 fen during the session. According to industry insiders, there is little hope for a turnaround in the near future.

(Rising Prices for Small Coins, Increased Copper Coin Value) Jiangnan small coins were priced at 6 mace, 2 fen, and 6 li in the morning session, a slight increase of half a li from the previous afternoon. 9,000 jiao were traded. The price suddenly rose again by 1 li in the afternoon session, reaching 6 mace, 2 fen, and 7 li, with 12,000 jiao traded. Guangdong small coins were priced at 6 mace, 2 fen, and 1.5 li in both the morning and afternoon sessions, an increase of 6 hao and 2 hu from the previous afternoon. 125,000 jiao were traded in the morning session and 15,000 jiao in the afternoon session. The value of copper coins increased by 1,300 cash, reaching 396,000 cash per thousand, with 41,100 strings of cash traded.

(Silent Silver Dollar Transactions and Settlements) "Silver dollar" settlements were quiet due to banks closing in the afternoon on the weekend. Chinese merchants settled 1.5 to 1.6 million in bills, foreign merchants settled 1.3 to 1.4 million in bills, special funds settled 2.2 to 2.3 million, advances were 1 million, final settlements were over 1.5 million, and various goods, foreign exchange taxes, and miscellaneous funds settled over 7.1 million. Security deposits traded over 1 million, withdrawals from warehouses were 800,000, settlements by money shops and silver firms were over 26 million, settlements of clearing house funds were over 3.2 million, remittances from various routes were over 700,000, and cash received was over 500,000. "Foreign dollar" exchange and bill transactions in the morning session reached 610,000, and 560,000 in the afternoon session. Banknote transactions were 85,000 in the morning session and 120,000 in the afternoon session. Off-exchange banknote transactions were 185,000 in the morning session and 210,000 in the afternoon session. Demand draft transactions were 70,000 in the morning session and 45,000 in the afternoon session. Interbank trading was 800,000 in the morning session and 400,000 in the afternoon session. Transactions between foreign accounts of various banks amounted to over 1.2 million. Banknotes retrieved were over 500,000, and banknotes issued were over 2.3 million. Two to three million in banknotes were sent to other locations, 600,000 in Yuan currency, and over 600,000 in foreign security deposits were traded. Settlements by foreign money shops and public firms were over 7.7 million, settlements of foreign clearing house funds were over 1.4 million, foreign dollar borrowing and lending inflows and outflows were over 1.9 million, and small money shop transactions were over 600,000.

Year-End Funds Being Collected

Yesterday, it was heard that the silver and money industry was eagerly purchasing banknotes, and banks were also issuing them in large quantities. Investigations revealed that this was for use in Hankou. These banknotes, specifically those issued by the Central Bank, Bank of China, Sze Ming Bank, and Xingye Bank, were intended for circulation in the Hankou market and for settling year-end goods payments. Therefore, the current silver dollar market in this city remains unchanged.

Securities

Financial Short-Term Bonds Rise Again to Limit Up

│More Declines Than Gains in Other Areas│

Yesterday (the 17th), the current market at the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange was deserted, with only a few types of securities opening throughout the day and sparse trading. The futures market was also less active than before. However, important bonds continued to see significant trading. The 20-year financial short-term bonds experienced extraordinary changes. Due to market demand and scarce selling, the price continued to rise sharply, from 55 yuan in the morning to 58 yuan at the limit up, an increase of 4 yuan from the previous day and a significant jump of 8 yuan over two days, the largest seen this year. The prices of other bonds tended to be stable, with fewer new purchases and sales than before, and more profit-taking transactions. Therefore, the overall market hovered around 6 or 7 jiao, slightly weaker than the previous day with sellers having a slight advantage. Total spot trading was 13,000 yuan, of which demobilization bonds accounted for 10,000 yuan, with the rest being only 1,000 yuan. Futures trading totaled 8.43 million yuan in the morning and afternoon sessions.

New York Stock Market Falls Back

According to a report from the Sun Fook Trading Company, the New York stock market fell back on Friday due to the disastrous drop in the Winnipeg wheat market and the continued weakness of US Steel stocks. The Winnipeg wheat market was weakened by rumors of renewed competition between Argentinian and Canadian wheat abroad, causing widespread panic and selling, leading to a price drop of three cents. However, the stock market's foundation remained solid, preventing a significant decline. Short sellers eventually covered their positions, resulting in mixed gains and losses. The current market situation appears to be quite good, as most stocks are held by genuine investors who are unwilling to sell easily. Total trading volume for the day was 910,000 shares. Tense Situation in the Yarn, Flower, and Cotton Yarn Market

丨Strong Speculative Appetite, Increasing Trading Volume丨

The cotton yarn market remains strong, and the situation is still tense. General retail investors are eagerly buying, with a strong desire to go long. However, some manufacturers, due to the current low prices of agricultural products, are also selling off large quantities of cotton yarn. They sold 15,000 to 16,000 bales in the morning session, and the market atmosphere eased slightly in the afternoon session. However, market sentiment remains tight. Spot yarn transactions are brisk, indicating the enthusiasm of speculators.

(Many Bids, Bulls and Bears Confront Each Other) Bidding in the morning session continued the momentum from the previous day, with eager buyers in the market. Fortunately, some manufacturers sold at the market price, slightly easing the market. As a result, each month increased by 1 mace. In the afternoon session, near-term contracts fell slightly by 3.6 qian, while distant contracts remained flat. Total trading volume for the day was 56,300 bales. Sales included: Geng Feng 5,500 bales, Chang Feng 4,550 bales, Yi Yu 2,500 bales, Da Chang 2,500 bales, Mei Ji 2,500 bales, Yuan Da 2,750 bales. Cotton Ginned Empty This Month

丨Market Transactions Lively丨

The cotton market surged in the morning, with general retailers chasing gains and increasing purchases. Due to the lack of goods for delivery for the amount sold by a certain manufacturer this month, retail shorts were panicked, and the market became increasingly brisk. The market's transactions are unusually lively. However, spot cotton prices are relatively flat, and factories are unwilling to purchase, with most adopting a "wait-and-see" attitude. Overseas cotton markets remain dull.

(Near-Term Zhengzhou Cotton Contracts Brisk) Zhengzhou cotton contracts opened higher in the morning session. Short covering drove up prices for near-term contracts, with distant contracts tightening. This month rose 4 qian, distant months rose 5 fen to 1 qian. In the afternoon, near-term contracts remained strong while distant contracts fell 5 fen to 1.5 qian. Total trading volume for the day was 163,300 dan. Grain and Flour Market Sees Significant Afternoon Surge

Grain rose in the morning, leading to anxiety. Near-term and distant months saw minor increases in li and fen. In the afternoon, buyers from Northern merchants, including Dalian merchants, had a strong appetite and aggressively bought up Fufeng flour at 5 fen above the listed price. New near-term contracts are mostly gone. The current price for three-week delivery flour is 1 liang 9 qian 5 fen. Spot flour factory prices have reached 2 . Near-term contracts were bought up for actual sales and by local customers. As a result, prices jumped repeatedly. At closing, this month rose sharply by 4 fen 25, next month rose by 3 fen 75, February rose by 2 fen 5, March rose by 75, and April/May each rose by 1 fen 25. Future prospects are still good, due to reports of Qixin halting production, leading to a shortage of spot flour. Furthermore, it is said that flour going to Dalian is being stockpiled by Japan and the puppet state for military use.

Fujian Merchants Purchase Over 1,000 Dan of New Lead Wire

Fujian merchants actively purchased new lead wire yesterday, buying a total of 1,200 to 1,300 dan. The specifications ranged from No. 12, 14, 16 to 25. Prices were 10 liang per dan for No. 12, 10 liang 1 qian 5 fen for No. 14, and an estimated 13 liang 7 qian 5 fen for No. 16 to 20, and 18 liang 5 qian for No. 21 to 25.

Free Talk

Short Story

On a River Steamer (2)

— Shi

But the old man, after careful consideration, knew that this matter was not easy to handle. First, he had no solid evidence against that person; second, he could not speak plainly, because the old man knew that those who acted along the Yangtze River had companions.

The next day, the river steamer was as calm and uneventful as the river water.

The old man observed the middle-aged man's actions more carefully. He even took the opportunity to talk to the young man in the next room, but all he could say were ordinary words of caution, unable to make the young man fully understand his meaning.

That night, the old man still could not sleep soundly, listening quietly to the sounds from the neighboring room all night, but everything seemed peaceful.

On the third day, the passengers on the ship were still alive and well.

So on the night of the third day, the old man felt more at ease, because by ten o'clock on the morning of the fourth day, the steamer would be able to reach the dock. He thought in bed:

"Maybe nothing will happen. Once I disembark, I can get rid of this responsibility on my conscience. If anything else happens, I won't know anything about it."

The old man drifted off to sleep until four or five o'clock when he suddenly woke up. The old man himself didn't understand why, but he felt a chill down his spine and his heart was trembling. He listened carefully and seemed to hear rustling sounds in the next room, but after a while, everything was quiet again, only the sound of the engine of the steamer traveling on the river. The old man was ice-cold and stiff all over, unable to move, as if a sandman was pressing down on him.

His breathing was rapid, and the old man waited quietly until dawn. There was a commotion on the ship, and many passengers were getting up to prepare to disembark. The old man mustered his courage and got out of bed. He ran to the door of the next room, hesitated, and finally knocked on the door. Inside, it sounded like someone was snoring deliberately. Someone opened the door, it was the middle-aged man. The old man looked into the room and saw no suspicious traces, but the young man was gone. The old man, barely supporting his trembling limbs, still said quietly:

"I've come to see the young man. He asked me yesterday to help him disembark today."

"He just went upstairs. He already told me that we would disembark together. Please don't bother yourself, old man," the middle-aged man replied calmly.

The old man agreed and walked away. He still worried about the young man and searched for him everywhere on the ship, but he couldn't find him. The old man thought:

"That young man is probably still lying quietly in that room, but I'm afraid he's already lifeless."

The old man, above his fear, also felt a kind of excitement. He had no absolute judgment on this matter, but he trusted his own judgment very much. He went to the ship's purser's room and saw an officer in uniform. He said to him:

The Difficulty of Translation

— Lin Yutang

In translation theory, there have always been two schools of thought: "literal translation" and "free translation," each with good reasons, leaving those who study translation at a loss. What is meant by literal translation and free translation is quite difficult to understand. Roughly speaking, literal translation means "writing directly" without modification. For example, a common English conversation, "How do you do? I am very well, thank you very much," literally translated would be:

Mr. So-and-so: How do you do?

Ms. So-and-so: I am very well. Thank you very much.

Or, "They walked arm in arm" literally translated should be: "They walked arm in arm." I find this method of translation very faithful, but it is inevitably too Westernized.

Therefore, I don't quite believe in literal translation, and I advocate another kind of translation. Whether this method is what people call "free translation" or not, there's no need to worry about it. The important thing is to determine what the original text refers to, and translate the corresponding Chinese words. For example, what Westerners call the "First Floor" is clearly the second floor, and in Chinese, it can only be translated as the second floor. Another example is "I have three brothers" can only be translated as "We are four brothers."

However, this method is also quite difficult. For material and concrete names, it is still easy. In abstract concepts, doubts often arise. For example, if a Western newspaper reports that more than 500 people attended a meeting somewhere, and the Chinese translation is "more than 500 people," the reader will inevitably get the impression of 50 or 60 people, so it should be translated as "3,000 people attended the meeting," so that the reader will get the impression of "maybe 400 or 500 people attended the meeting." Another example is that the appointed time "exactly 7 o'clock" should be translated as "5:30 PM," so that everyone attending will definitely achieve the effect of "exactly 7 o'clock." This has been repeatedly tested and proven.

When translating from Chinese into Western languages, even more detailed consideration should be given, otherwise the true meaning will be lost. For example, Chinese high school graduates who go to Berlin to study are admitted to universities as soon as they present their diplomas, precisely because the words "high school" are mistranslated as "Middle School," and Germans believe that "Middle School" is equivalent to the German "Gymnasium," so Chinese high school graduates get too much of an advantage.

In addition, I have thought of a few more examples for reference:

The Chinese word for "train" should be translated into the Western language as "Wheelbarrow."

Military vehicles, often with guards on duty, are not easy to translate, "tank" may be used.

"University president" can be translated as "Shroff" (i.e., the street debt collector hired by foreign firms).

"A small drink" should be translated as "Big Peast," and the Western word "Dinner" can only be translated as "a small drink."

"Wife" can be translated as "Housekeeper"; "concubine" can be translated as "lover"; "family" can be translated as "hotel" or "Boardingbouse."

"Humorous" can be translated as "Trying to be funny."

These are just a few examples, and the rest can be inferred by analogy.

On the Way to a Funeral

— Zhao Jiabi

Just before the train started, a chaotic sound poured in through the carriage door, followed by three women and two men who chose seats near the window, forcibly squeezing into them by pushing aside people's clothing. This group of people was dressed casually, as if they had rushed out of their homes without bothering to dress up. Each person's face was covered with a layer of extremely sad black clouds that had cast a shadow over their fate. At the corners of the women's eyes, traces of tears remained, and the older woman's red, swollen eyelids were still filled with heavy tears. They had been temporarily distracted from their heartfelt grief by the crowds and the urgency of getting on the train. When the stationmaster's whistle pierced the passengers' eardrums, everyone remembered the mission of this journey. In their recollection of how the deceased brother, suffering from lung disease in Hangzhou, had hoped that his family would wait for him to recover so they could visit the lake together, the mother, brothers, and sisters were now unable to make it in time to mourn his death. The old woman was the first to cry out, and the others followed, covering their mouths with handkerchiefs as they sobbed. Everyone felt as if they were facing the oppression of "death," and the value of life was impossible to estimate.

After the train passed Jiaxing, the carriage gradually quieted down. The only sound breaking the silence was the rhythmic rolling of the wheels on the rails. The passengers leaned back their heads, each lost in their own dreams. The group of mourners no longer needed to use the ends of their arms to maintain their balance, and sat comfortably, their spirits living a different kind of life. Two of them leaned against the window, gazing at the villages and mountains that flashed by outside the train. Because these two young women had not traveled this route in a long time, they found the lambs in the green grass and the croaking in the ponds particularly interesting. Their faces were angled towards the window, waiting for something new and strange to pass by so they could be the first to turn their heads to admire it. In addition to the sound of the train wheels, one could vaguely hear them arguing about past Qingming Festival nights when they visited the lake. In their memories, they recalled the joyous scene of secretly leaning on their lovers' shoulders in the moonlight, and with their eyes closed, they still felt a burst of intoxication with "life." Their brothers, sitting on the opposite chairs, also faced the window, but shielded their faces with newspapers. They were enjoying the joyous urban life in their fantasies, reading the local supplements: the swaying curves, the soaring fox trots, and Garbo's husky voice. The rhythmic sound of the wheels sent into their ears instinctively made their toes tap along with the waltz beat. The joy of "life" occupied their entire spirits, and they threw all their sorrows into the land of forgetting. The remaining old woman leaned her head against her daughter's back, swaying up and down with the vibrations of the train. Although her eyelids were equally red and swollen, she had fallen soundly asleep. Although she was not as good at forgetting as the young people, she did, at least for a moment of unconsciousness during sleep, shake off the oppression of "death."

The train wheels kept moving forward, carrying five souls to a funeral. They had initially been so frightened by death that they lacked the courage to face "life," but time overcame emotion, and the desire for "life" finally occupied the entire world. In addition to giving mankind various virtues, God gave humans the ability to forget, allowing them to regain balance from extreme sorrow.

The train moved forward, and the active life of humanity relies on this "forgetful" nature to extend into the endless future!

Strange Tales of Australian Aborigines (2)

— Wei Han

After the Kurnai Aborigines performed this kind of ritual in public, the newcomer had to live in seclusion in the bushes for several months. During this period, they were monitored by ascetics who watched over them, doing this and that work to hone their self-discipline. Generally speaking, they were very reluctant to let people see such secrets; therefore, it was very difficult to see them. Therefore, this ritual seemed to have a very profound moral effect. When the period of asceticism was about to end, someone would go out to report the news, and then hundreds of people would gather at this sacred place. The ascetic, after a long period of solitary life, was then able to join the crowds; therefore, he was extremely stimulated, and in terms of emotion, there was a sense of soaring ambition. Many crowds then danced and sang vigorously around the ascetic.

At this time, the newcomer would be given moral and religious teachings. The teachings were: do not be willful; if you get something yourself, you must distribute it to friends; you must live peacefully; you must take male and female relationships very seriously; absolutely do not eat forbidden things; you must listen to the advice of the elders, and you must absolutely obey their words. Also, above us, there exists an all-knowing and all-powerful

Withered String Sounds

— Ye Jifeng

Every day, every day, she always walks past my building.

Every day, every day, I always watch her walk past my building from upstairs.

In the silent dusk, pale streetlights, and dark shadows of trees, the coolness of early autumn flows.

In the touching homesickness of early autumn evenings, the mournful sound of her sanxian is like a bird without a nest to return to in the evening, wandering in the silent air of dusk.

There is no sheet music, no singing to accompany it, and it is not a sweeping, long performance, only intermittent string sounds strummed casually, but in these fragmented string sounds, infinite sorrow seems to be unconsciously revealed.

A gray-white upper garment, black pants, hair and face indistinctly blurred into a ball, dragging a long, heavy black shadow cast by the streetlights from the gaps between the trees, slowly disappearing at the corner of the road. It seems not to be walking, but moving slowly in a mechanical way.

The figure disappears into the darkness at the corner of the road, and the intermittent string sounds still linger in the silent air of dusk.

Imagining twenty or perhaps thirty years ago, the person drifting on the streets today might have been a stunning beauty who captivated all living beings, but the ruthless years, listening to the turning of the wheel of life, generously withered this masterpiece of creation. Time flows eastward, and the string sounds may still be the string sounds of the past, but the hand plucking the strings is definitely not the slender hand of the past.

In the dusk, leaning on the quiet upstairs, from the chaotic string sounds, watching her wriggling black shadow, I cannot help but feel pity for the ephemeral nature of life.

Every day, every day, she walks past my building like this.

Every day, every day, I watch her walk past my building like this.

Several days of autumn rain have added to the homesickness and melancholy of the traveler's upstairs. Waking up from a nap, watching the rainy streets in the dusk, the lights remain, but in the low, damp air, there is no longer the sound of her strings.

On the first night after the rain cleared, a few fallen leaves blown down by the autumn wind were still wet and stuck to the sloping steps, not flying up. After the streetlights were lit one by one, I leaned lonely on the window. I knew that the string sounds, separated for a few days, would definitely meet again in the shade of the trees tonight.

But the night colors in the shade of the trees gradually deepened, the water accumulated on the sides of the street reflected the autumn stars in the sky, and under the pale streetlights, after the sound of cars subsided, I never saw that heavy black shadow move past again.

On the second night after the rain cleared, the disappearance of the string sounds remained the same.

The fallen leaves in the autumn wind are increasing day by day. Leaning against the upstairs in the evening, facing the desolate new cold, I cannot help but add an unnamed lingering feeling in addition to homesickness.

The autumn wind has been even stronger these few days. Several places on the two trees outside the window have revealed bare trunks. Under the streetlights in the evening, there are only the rustling sounds of colorful fallen leaves, and her string sounds have never been heard again.

The autumn light is old, and the withered string sounds have probably grown old along with this withered autumn light. I sighed in this way.

Every day, every day, I still lean on my upstairs like this.

Every day, every day, I no longer see her walk past my building.

God, He can make it rain, make all things revive, and His voice is thunder. One must try hard to please God on weekdays, otherwise, one cannot ascend to heaven after death. These Aborigines are deeply convinced that practical rituals can produce mystical and supreme effects. When a child finishes the ritual and comes out of the jungle, the first thing he thinks about is getting married.

There is no word for "father" among Australian Aborigines: they call fathers and uncles "Ukapelli" and mothers and aunts "Kaka." Because in the past there was no individual marriage system among these races, all men were common husbands of all women: and this term may be a relic of this so-called promiscuous marriage era. This promiscuous marriage system has now been abolished. Although marriage is now free, first cousins (such as male cousins and female cousins) cannot marry: as for second cousins, it does not matter.

In choosing a wife, everyone is subject to various racial regulations, and the simplest of these is the Kurnai Aborigines. Their race is divided into five factions, and one faction is divided into nineteen parties. The parties are a collection of groups scattered in various places. A group has a family, an old man and his children and grandchildren live together. When choosing a wife, it is absolutely forbidden to marry blood relatives, and everyone cannot marry within their own party, they must choose someone from another party, which is called exogamy.

Long Novel

The Crossroads of Era and Love 18

— Zhang Ziping

You can take it to my room for me.

He said as he walked out of the back door of the Zeng's house. On the road, he was still hoping that Mrs. Tsuruko could see this card.

"It's really inexplicable. Why is Mrs. Tsuruko so close to that old Japanese ghost? Could he be her lover? I heard that in Japanese male and female relationships, it's not uncommon for the age difference to be ten or twenty years."

Because of this matter, he seemed unable to be at ease all day today. He thought that he was not in the mood to listen to lectures today. Not only did he feel a kind of unease in his heart, but he also felt a kind of grief that had no name.

"Today is December 2nd, and the Ren family is hosting a wine party on the 5th, which is four days away. If it were tonight, it would be nice to go back later. I really don't want to see that Mrs. Tsuruko! No, I don't want to see those Japanese ghosts!"

The more he thought about it, the more indignant and heartbroken he felt. Sitting in the third-class tram, he really wanted to cry.

"If I really shed tears for this Japanese woman, then my tears would be too cheap!"

Reason and emotion fought in his chest for a while, and the trolleybus stopped at the terminal.

After getting off the tram, he hesitated for a while about whether to walk or hire a rickshaw. He felt that his outlook on life was a little different from yesterday. Yesterday, although he was a bit pessimistic about the world, he still held the tenet of being hardworking, thrifty, and striving to be a good person. But today, after seeing that old Japanese ghost, his old outlook on life suddenly wavered, and he became disheartened about everything in the world, as disheartened as the gray and white color of the sky above his head. As soon as he thought of Mrs. Tsuruko, he hated her so much that he gnashed his teeth and hurriedly shook his head. But sometimes he wanted to copy down a large collection of poems like the one written by Han Hesheng in *Traces of Flowers and the Moon*, "Scratching my head in confusion, I want to ask the heavens," and send it to Mrs. Tsuruko to read. If after reading it, she "had tears welling up in her eyes and dropping down," then that would relieve my anger.

"She is a Japanese woman, how would she understand Chinese poetry! Isn't that like playing the lute to a cow?"

Thinking of this, his heart turned cold again.

A group of rickshaw pullers surrounded him.

"Want a rickshaw?"

"Going to ×× University, want a rickshaw?"

Unconsciously, he jumped into a rickshaw and sat down.

"Forget it. What's the meaning of life! Why bother walking to save ten or twenty cents, making my legs sore and out of breath. I want to change my old outlook on life."

He paid attention and saw that there were also twos and threes of classmates and teachers, each sitting in a rickshaw, braving the cold wind, and speeding towards the university.

Haiquan got out of the rickshaw and had just stepped into the outer gate when he heard the clanging of the class bell. He hurried towards the classroom. The first class today was Professor Wang's differential calculus, and he was a famous teacher who started classes early. Haiquan walked to the entrance of the classroom and saw that there were two or three classmates still standing in the corridor outside the classroom, knowing that Professor Wang had not yet arrived, so he was relieved.
